Current Commentary

Preparing Former President Li's State Funeral 33

— Capital

The passing of Huangpi (Li Yuanhong) has been over seven years. We always admire this president, who was known for his integrity and purity of character. Recently, the National Government issued a clear order to prepare for a state funeral and appointed Zhang Qun, Chairman of the Hubei Provincial Government, to oversee the arrangements. Moreover, the Executive Yuan meeting the day before yesterday decided to allocate an additional 10,000 yuan for the state funeral expenses, to facilitate its swift completion and avoid delays. This clearly shows the central government's intention not to forget the sages and to praise them, and it is also a deserved reward for Huangpi's dedication to the Republic of China. Those who reflect on Huangpi's past achievements should feel a sense of righteousness and express their joy. Furthermore, we believe that if the state funeral for former President Li were only motivated by rewarding merit and honoring accomplishments, it would not fully reveal the true meaning of this event. We must select the magnanimous and brilliant aspects of Li Gong's life and deeds that are worthy of eternal remembrance, repeatedly emphasize and appreciate them. Then, the impression given by the state funeral will have a more profound significance.

Li Gong was a military man with a long history of service, bearing the merit and reputation of leading the Wuchang Uprising in 1911, a feat recorded in history. He received widespread respect and reached the highest position. However, due to his kind and generous nature, he struggled to restore order. He remained low-profile and unassuming, transcending worldly affairs. Judging by the weight of the nation's trust, he may not have fully satisfied the expectations of the people. However, considering his self-discipline and unyielding integrity, he was undoubtedly an outstanding figure of his time. How can he not only be admired by his contemporaries but also serve as a model for today? At the beginning of Yuan Shikai's administration, sycophants competed to offer flattery, and many people were eager to seek personal gain and used nominal positions as rewards and official ranks as incentives. Corrupt practices prevailed, and it became difficult to distinguish right from wrong. Seeing the danger of the times, Li Gong deeply deplored the corruption of officials. He sent letters to Yuan Shikai and the heads of various departments, expressing his sincere advice and offering thorough admonitions. He also telegraphed various provinces to denounce the malpractices of the time. Newspapers at the time published his words widely, shocking the entire nation. Later, when Yuan Shikai attempted to become emperor, Li Gong immediately resigned and prepared to leave. Yuan tried to lure him with the title of Prince Wuyi, but Li firmly refused. When Hongxian's meritorious officials coerced him to attend court, Li swore to resist until death. His unwavering sense of righteousness left even Yuan Shikai helpless. Regarding his personal choices, he always prioritized loyalty to Qingjie (the Qing Dynasty). From the Wuchang Uprising to the establishment of order, he only took twenty gold coins to provide for the expenses of his horse. When he became president, he repeatedly reduced the expenses of the presidential palace and refused the supply from the Chongwenmen Customs. These are all clear examples of his character. Today, government officials are striving to cultivate integrity, eliminate corruption, and punish corrupt officials, as has been repeatedly proclaimed. However, there are still few officials who dare to speak out, and the trend of seeking personal gain is difficult to curb. The concern for the integrity of the nation in times of upheaval should be a priority for those in power. Therefore, how can we not deeply admire and emulate a former president who was so honest, self-respecting, upright, and unyielding? The nation faces difficult times, and there is a pressing need for reform. The gradual improvement of morals will begin here.

British and French Naval Experts Hold First Meeting at British Admiralty; U.S. Secretary of the Navy Secretly Orders Accelerated Shipbuilding; Japanese Telegram Claims Britain and the U.S. Plan Joint Action Against Japan 34

(London) British and French naval experts held their first joint meeting this morning at the British Admiralty to prepare for the London Naval Conference, which will open on December 2. They discussed ways to enable Britain and France to cooperate in the Mediterranean in accordance with Article 16, Paragraph 3 of the League of Nations Covenant, especially on how the French Navy would take over when the British Navy withdraws its warships from the Mediterranean, and the issue of the British Navy using French naval ports. However, this Anglo-French naval cooperation will only be effective when sanctions are implemented. The French experts attending the naval conference are Admiral Dego and Captain Louis. (Havas, 30th)

(Tokyo) The actions of Britain and the United States towards Japan before the opening of the disarmament conference are attracting much attention. According to information from the Havas News Agency, Ambassador Sato in France reported to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs that the U.S. government, in its reply to the League of Nations regarding the Italian sanctions issue, reiterated its consistent stance of upholding peace and supporting Britain's position. This was decided after a week of secret negotiations between Britain and the United States. Therefore, Britain agreed to maintain the U.S. position of opposing equality with Japan and opposing reducing the tonnage of battleships as the price for supporting Britain's position. (Dentsu, 30th)

(Washington) Secretary of the Navy Swanson today secretly ordered the directors of naval shipyards to accelerate the completion of shipbuilding plans in order to reach the naval strength limited by the treaty as soon as possible. He stated that the 524 ships must be launched, which would also provide jobs for many unemployed Americans. (Guomin, 29th)

(Washington) Rear Admiral Stoddard, former commander of the U.S. Asiatic Fleet and now commander of the Third Naval District, published an article in the Naval Institute Proceedings today, stating that after the European situation stabilizes, Western naval powers will seek to restore their power in the East. He also said that countries will engage in extreme shipbuilding competition due to Germany's naval recovery. In this situation, Germany will build at least five battleships and two aircraft carriers, rendering the British fleet powerless. France and Italy will certainly not be left behind, and the U.S. and Japan will actively replenish their fleets. Japan will act freely in China due to the unrest in Europe. If so, the powers with significant interests in the East will certainly not be willing to give up their right to speak on Far Eastern affairs. (Guomin, 29th)

(London) The Admiralty recently signed a contract with a large machine factory in Birkenhead to install new engines on the battlecruiser Renown. The Renown is currently in the Strait of Gibraltar, built in 1916, with a displacement of 26,000 tons, armor up to 9 inches thick, and equipped with six 15-inch guns and fifteen 4-inch guns. The battleship Hood, with a displacement of 42,000 tons, is also in the Strait of Gibraltar and is one of the largest warships in the British Navy. (Havas, 29th)

(Tokyo) The Japanese Navy's minelayer "Okinoshima," built by the Harima Shipbuilding Company, and the warship "Ryujo," built by the Kure Naval Arsenal, will be launched on November 15 and 23 respectively. The Emperor will send Military Counselor Prince Fushimi to attend the ceremonies. (Havas, 30th)

Explosion at Japanese Akaike Coal Mine; 77 Bodies Recovered 35

Fukuoka: After the explosion at the Akaike Coal Mine in Fukuoka, 77 bodies of workers have been recovered. Rescue teams are still continuing to search for the remaining bodies. (Domei, 30th)

Page 6

Britain, France, and Italy Strive for Rapprochement; Paris Peace Talks Now Move to Geneva; Hull and Laval Discuss Jointly; Drummond and Mussolini Talk at Length; Content of Peace Plan Reported by French Newspapers 36

(London) British and French experts are now striving to find the greatest possible concessions that can be offered to Mussolini while adhering to the principles of the League of Nations, in order to end the Italian-Ethiopian war as soon as possible. However, it is widely believed that the talks currently underway in Paris are highly fluid. Officials claim that their purpose is to decide how to respond to Italy's proposals. It is expected that Italy's proposals will be submitted to the League of Nations Council within the next few days. (Reuters, 30th)

(Rome) British Ambassador to Italy Drummond met with Mussolini for a long time today. This meeting is regarded here as "most important," but its content remains confidential. (Guomin, 29th)

(Rome) Mussolini discussed with British Ambassador to Rome Sir Eric Drummond for an hour today. The nature of their conversation has not been disclosed. According to a government spokesperson, diplomatic contacts are still ongoing, but there have been no discussions regarding proposals to resolve the Italian-Ethiopian war. (Reuters, 29th)

(Rome) British sources say that both Britain and Italy are now striving for the success of negotiations. It is generally believed that the Prime Minister and Drummond have studied the various elements for resolving the dispute, but their content is quite different from the conditions revealed in the newspapers last week. (Havas, 29th)

(Paris) Prime Minister and Foreign Minister Laval received the Italian Ambassador to France Cerutti at the Ministry of Foreign Affairs this morning. (Havas, 30th)

(Rome) In recent days, there has been widespread concern that Britain and France have reached an agreement to implement sanctions against Italy and are seeking to resolve the Italian-Ethiopian dispute on a basis that Italy cannot accept. Now, these concerns have been dispelled. Since British Ambassador to Italy Drummond met with Italian Prime Minister Mussolini yesterday afternoon, government officials have announced that direct negotiations between Britain and Italy have resumed. It is believed that Britain will soon present Italy with proposals to resolve the dispute. (Havas, 30th)

(Paris) According to the Petit Parisien today, the content of the Anglo-French peace plan is as follows:

(1) Appoint an Italian as an advisor to the Ethiopian Emperor.

(2) Appoint an Italian as the local administrator of a border province of Ethiopia.

(3) Deploy "foreign troops" manned by Italians.

(4) Cede the Ogaden province to Italy. The boundaries of the entire Tigray province and the Danakil region will be determined later.

(5) Provide Ethiopia with a corridor to the sea. (Guomin, 29th)

(Paris) According to the Petit Parisien, although British and French experts have recently drafted proposals in Paris to resolve the Italian-Ethiopian dispute, they have not yet been accepted by Britain and France. They will now be jointly discussed by British Foreign Secretary Hoare and French Prime Minister Laval in Geneva. The content of these draft proposals is to implement the international assistance plan recommended by the Five-Power Committee of the League of Nations Council on September 18 in central Ethiopia. For the border provinces of Ethiopia, it is proposed that the Ethiopian Emperor hire Italian advisors stationed in the Ethiopian capital, so that Italy can exercise administrative power in these provinces. However, the southern provinces of Harar and Ogaden will not be completely annexed by Italy. Ethiopia will only cede a portion of the Ogaden province to Italy in exchange for a seaport in Italian Eritrea. The newspaper also said that the British government's position is to firmly adhere to the actions taken by the League of Nations. Therefore, the proposals drafted by the British and French experts may not be directly accepted. It is likely that the League of Nations will use the recommendations of the Five-Power Committee and the recommendations of the British and French experts as a basis to formulate a new plan to resolve the Italian-Ethiopian dispute before it can be accepted. (Havas, 30th)

(Paris) The Paris Soir today published an authorized article on the progress of peace talks to resolve the Italian-Ethiopian war, stating that British and French representatives met last Sunday and agreed on several proposals to be submitted to the British government and telegraphed to Rome. It is heard that these proposals allow Italy to rule several provinces of Ethiopia, but do not include Harar, the holy city of Aksum, or western Ethiopia, because the Ethiopian Emperor will certainly oppose this cession. (Reuters, 29th)

Hoare Confirms Anglo-French Peace Plan; Denies Collusion with Italy 37

(London) British Foreign Secretary Hoare gave a speech to voters in his constituency of Chelsea this afternoon, dispelling the strange and ridiculous atmosphere created by some political critics regarding the peace talks. He said that some people mistakenly suspect that "we are now abandoning the League of Nations and colluding with Italy behind its back." This kind of concern is unfounded. Hoare confirmed that Britain and France are currently discussing the Italian-Ethiopian peace talks in Paris, saying that Pederson, the director of the Abyssinian division of the Foreign Office, is currently discussing some complex details with French Foreign Office officials. Nothing has been disclosed yet. If there is a decision, it will be reported to the League of Nations as soon as possible. The Foreign Secretary reiterated that any resolution must be achieved within the framework of the League of Nations and satisfy the League of Nations, Italy, and Ethiopia. Everything is transparent, and there is no cause for suspicion. (Reuters, 30th)

(Paris) Today, the reactions of various countries to the peace plan drafted by the British and French experts are mixed. London is keeping silent about it, but there is much speculation about the meeting between British Ambassador Drummond and Mussolini in Rome. Geneva believes that any compromise is difficult to accept by both Italy and Ethiopia, as well as the member states of the League of Nations. Rome declares, "We are not very optimistic about such plans." As for the Ethiopian capital, officials reiterated their previous position, namely the Ethiopian Emperor's statement that Ethiopia refuses to cede Tigray. (Guomin, 29th)

(Rome) Today, the Italian newspaper Il Giornale d'Italia published an article by the famous Italian writer Gaeta, expressing disappointment at the failure of the recent peace talks, saying that Britain and France, because of the great sacrifices Italy made in the European war, have resumed their Versailles cooperation in order to curb Italy's necessary colonial expansion. Italy must disregard the friendship of the two countries and other countries for its own needs and interests. (Reuters, 29th)

Britain Notifies Italy of Reduction of Mediterranean Fleet to Ease the Situation; Result of Anglo-French Cooperation 38

(London) According to reliable sources, the government has decided to instruct Ambassador Drummond in Italy to notify the Italian government that Britain has decided to withdraw several British warships stationed in the Mediterranean. This decision is the result of an agreement between Britain and France, and its purpose is to ease the situation. (Havas, 29th)

(London) In the Admiralty's opinion, a portion of the British Mediterranean Fleet needs to be recalled to the UK, and French warships can take over their duties. On the 28th of this month, France replied to the British note, allowing the British Navy to receive assistance from the French Navy if it is attacked while implementing sanctions. Subsequently, the two countries continued to hold talks and reached an agreement on the following two points: (1) If British warships in the Mediterranean are recalled to the UK, they will be taken over by French warships. Because of this agreement, Britain will now notify Italy of the withdrawal of several warships stationed in the Mediterranean. (2) The British Navy can use several French naval bases. The detailed arrangements for this will be discussed by British and French naval experts before the naval conference opens on December 2. (Havas, 29th)

(Geneva) British Foreign Secretary Hoare and French Prime Minister and Foreign Minister Laval are currently discussing how the two countries should help each other if they are attacked by Italy while implementing sanctions. Regarding this, France argues that if its land borders are attacked, Britain should immediately provide assistance, especially in the air force. (Havas, 29th)

(London) Some political figures have stated that the British War Office and Admiralty have agreed to offer special guarantees to France as the basis for a general appeasement of Europe. Lord Rothermere, a key figure in the Conservative Party, previously advocated a defensive alliance with France. This proposal is now being promoted again. Regarding the Italian-Ethiopian dispute, it is heard that negotiations are being held between Britain and France in order to draft joint proposals to be submitted to both Italy and Ethiopia. It is generally hoped that Italian Prime Minister Mussolini will gradually understand the dangers of financial and economic sanctions, and his attitude will no longer be as firm as before. (Havas, 29th)

(London) According to the diplomatic correspondent of the Daily Telegraph, key staff members of the French Army, Navy, and Air Force will arrive here today from Paris to discuss the naval conference and other issues specifically related to Europe with British experts. It is heard that British Ambassador to Italy Drummond notified Italian Prime Minister Mussolini of this matter yesterday. (Havas, 30th)

Official Gazette of Rome Announces Completion of Preparations; Offensive to Be Launched Soon 39

(Rome) The government recently issued a communiqué stating that General De Bono, High Commissioner for East Africa, telegraphed that Italian patrols encountered and repelled a unit of Ethiopian troops yesterday. Several chiefs of Tigray province later surrendered to the Italian authorities in Adowa. At present, all preparations for transportation of supplies and food have been completed. (Havas, 30th)

Italian Front: Italian troops are expected to launch a major offensive soon on both the northern and southern fronts. The northern front aims at the city of Magala, and the southern front aims to attack the town of Gorahai. Recent Italian reconnaissance has proved that the villages between Adigrat and Magala on the northern front can be easily occupied by Italian troops, allowing artillery to advance through these villages towards Magala. On the southern front, General Graziani, commander-in-chief of the Italian Somaliland front, is preparing everything to attack the town of Gorahai. (Havas, 30th)

(Rome) The Ministry of War announced today that Italian Dubat (native troops) defeated Ethiopian troops between Sheray and Grahai, capturing 722 rifles. The number of casualties has not been estimated, but it is said that after this battle, Italian troops advanced victoriously and occupied Ethiopian territory to the banks of the Takaze River. (Guomin, 29th)

(London) Italian troops on both the northern and southern fronts are preparing to advance into central Ethiopia. British military experts are deeply skeptical about whether the Italian troops will eventually achieve victory. Experts claim that General De Bono, commander of the northern front, commanding three divisions of 180,000 troops, is now fighting against the terrain and the weather, which will subject the Italian military strategy to a major test. They admit that capturing Magala is indeed easy, but after capturing it, the advancing troops will encounter real difficulties. The left wing of the northern army is currently based in Adigrat. British experts state that this army is mostly composed of irregular troops and surrendered Ethiopian troops and Italian Eritrean troops, with a heterogeneous military organization. This army is closest to Quqdaft, but the terrain is extremely rugged, with many peaks and deep ravines. The central and winged armies are equipped with tanks and artillery, but they must cross mountains 9,000 feet high and pass through desolate areas where Ethiopian guerrillas may be lurking to attack. Experts therefore state that road construction is the most important task for the Italian troops. (Guomin, 29th)

(Rome) According to a report from the Italian Southern Front headquarters today, Italian tanks attacked the Ethiopian positions in front of Hilaf on the right wing of the Italian troops currently advancing along the Webi Shebelle River, assisted by bombing aircraft. Due to rain, visibility was poor, so the attack was not very convenient, but the goal was still achieved. The Ethiopian troops are still retreating along the Ogaden line, apparently planning to defend the mountains. (Reuters, 29th)

Italian Front: Italian troops have now established contact between Italian Somaliland and Eritrea. Two columns of Italian troops departing from Somaliland, one having crossed the Wardair and advanced into the sparsely populated sandy mining area, the other divided into two teams, advancing separately towards the town of Gorahai along the Webi Giarer River. The Ethiopian troops in that area are soldiers from the Amhara and Shoa tribes, all carrying their families and slaves. On the Eritrean front, there are small skirmishes between Italian and Ethiopian troops along the Setit River. On October 8 and 9, 3,000 Ethiopian troops attempted to cross the Setit River and enter Eritrean territory, but were unsuccessful. There were many casualties on both sides in this battle. It is heard that there are currently about 10,000 Ethiopian troops concentrated in the Setit River basin. (Havas, 30th)

Ethiopian Capital: It was learned today that senior Ethiopian generals have apparently allowed Italian troops on the northern front to penetrate 125 miles into the central highlands. The first major battle will take place in the mountains 100 miles east of Lake Tana, the source of the Blue Nile. Residents are now fleeing Magala, which is only 12 miles from the town. Officials believe that the claim that 20,000 Ethiopian troops have been killed on the northern front is unfounded. So far, the Italian troops have only encountered guerrilla resistance. (Guomin, 29th)

U.S. First Lady's 16 Speeches Earn $72,000; All Donated to Charity 40

(New York) News today: First Lady Roosevelt recently made 16 radio broadcast speeches, each lasting 15 minutes, earning a total of $72,000. Mrs. Roosevelt has donated the entire amount to a certain charity. It is said that President Roosevelt's annual salary is only $75,000, so Mrs. Roosevelt can be proud of herself. (Guomin, 29th)

The League of Nations Sanctions Committee Reconvenes Today; Italy Still Sends Observers; Two Have Arrived in Geneva from Rome; More Countries Continue to Join Sanctions 41

(Geneva) The League of Nations General Assembly's Sanctions Plan Adjustment Committee is scheduled to meet at 5:00 PM on the 31st of this month. The Eighteen-Nation Subcommittee is scheduled to hold a preliminary meeting tomorrow morning. The two observers sent by the Italian government to attend the meeting, one being Rosa, the Director of League of Nations Affairs at the Italian Ministry of Foreign Affairs, and the other being Marcia, will arrive here this afternoon from Rome. British Minister Without Portfolio Eden and French League of Nations affairs expert Massigli, along with the Director of Commercial Affairs at the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, Coulondre, will arrive tomorrow. British Foreign Secretary Hoare and French Prime Minister and Foreign Minister Laval will not arrive in Geneva until the morning of November 1st. (Havas Dispatch, 30th)

(Paris) The cabinet held a State Council meeting at 10:00 AM, during which Prime Minister and Foreign Minister Laval reported on the diplomatic situation and the upcoming Sanctions Committee meeting and Eighteen-Nation Subcommittee meeting in Geneva. The meeting adjourned at 11:30 AM. (Havas Dispatch, 30th)

(London) Prime Minister Baldwin met with Foreign Secretary Hoare this morning to discuss matters. Minister Without Portfolio Eden departed for Paris this afternoon, en route to Geneva. (Havas Dispatch, 30th)

(Geneva) The deadline for member states of the League of Nations to submit their responses regarding the sanctions issue was yesterday. The League of Nations Secretariat published the following statistics for these responses: A total of 40 countries have implemented an embargo on military supplies to Italy; 36 countries have adopted financial and economic sanctions; and 18 countries have accepted economic assistance to countries participating in the sanctions. Among the countries that submitted their responses last, China and Yugoslavia have indicated their acceptance of all measures recommended by the League of Nations. Portugal has accepted economic sanctions and mutual assistance, but has expressed some reservations regarding financial sanctions and the embargo on military supplies. Canada and Venezuela have indicated their acceptance of financial and economic sanctions. (Havas Dispatch, 30th)

Ottawa Canadian Prime Minister Mackenzie King recently announced that the government is prepared to implement sanctions against Italy. He stated that the government has not accepted any obligations regarding military sanctions, so this should not be an issue. Although the government has approved the sanctions measures this time, this should not be taken as a precedent for future actions. In other words, if future international disputes arise that necessitate sanctions, the government will consider the matter separately at that time. As for the present situation, the Canadian government has decided to take appropriate measures immediately to prevent Italy from issuing public bonds in Canada, prohibit loans to Italy, and prohibit the export of arms, ammunition, and military supplies to Italy. However, the prohibition of Italian goods from entering Canada and the prohibition of exporting essential military industrial materials to Italy will be coordinated with the member states of the League of Nations. (Havas News Agency Dispatch, 29th)

Helsinki The government has decided to participate in financial and economic sanctions against Italy and has notified the Secretary-General of the League of Nations, Avenol. (Havas Dispatch, 29th)

Mexico The Senate and House of Representatives recently passed a bill granting President Cárdenas the power to implement economic and financial sanctions against Italy in accordance with the resolutions of the League of Nations. The following items are prohibited from being sent to Italy: heavy livestock such as donkeys and horses, rubber, iron, aluminum, manganese, nickel, chromium, tin, and specially tempered steel. According to Foreign Minister Baudequi, Mexico is only concerned with fulfilling its duties and implementing sanctions, regardless of any losses that may result from doing so. (Havas Dispatch, 29th)

(London) It is not hoped here that a basis for peace can be established before the League of Nations implements its boycott. However, Britain and France may adopt a "peace offensive" to bring Italy into line. Anglo-French naval cooperation in the Mediterranean has now been fully confirmed. French Foreign Minister Laval has clearly notified British Foreign Secretary Hoare of the scope of cooperation. At the same time, the British Ambassador to Italy, Drummond, has also notified Mussolini. The Anglo-French peace proposals can serve as a benchmark for future Italian demands. It is heard that Britain has endorsed this peace plan but does not believe Mussolini will accept it. Britain does not wish to put Italy in a difficult position. The government is now open-minded and awaiting further proposals from Italy. (National Telegram, 30th)

Prices Soar in Rome; Thirty-Six Businesses Ordered to Close 42

(Rome) The wives and children of soldiers killed in action during the European War will organize a committee to encourage the people to resist the sanctions imposed by the member states of the League of Nations. They will go door-to-door in Rome to persuade people to limit consumption for the sake of the country. Official statistics show that the cost of living in September was only 0.28% higher than in August and 4.24% higher than in the same month last year. In the past month, 36 food businesses were ordered to close due to excessively high prices. (Reuters Dispatch, 30th)

(Rome) Italy is consolidating its economic position today, preparing to wage a trade war against countries that have implemented economic sanctions. The government has issued orders to restrict the consumption of meat, electricity, coal, and other necessities, while the public has launched a movement to promote domestic goods. (National Telegram, 29th)

(Rome) During the period of sanctions imposed by the League of Nations, Italy has decided that the state will control the national economy. The methods are divided into three categories: (1) Reduce consumption; (2) Control international trade and reduce imports; and (3) Increase domestic production. The following measures have been taken regarding the first item, reducing consumption: (1) Force public buses to convert to carbon gas fuel, every week; (2) Prohibit the sale of meat for two days each week; (3) Require each restaurant to serve only one dish per customer once a week; (4) Limit the length of newspapers and magazines. In addition, to save fuel, the government has set fixed working hours for government agencies, from 8:00 AM to 12:30 PM and from 3:00 PM to 6:00 PM. Government agencies should first reduce the length and number of their publications. The size of official letterhead and envelopes used by government agencies will also be reduced. (Havas, 29th)

(Rome) The government has begun a nationwide campaign to urge people to stop buying all non-essential foreign goods. In addition, the government will soon issue an order prohibiting the import of goods from countries imposing sanctions on Italy. Even if the sanctions are lifted in the future, the import of goods from these countries will be prohibited unless they purchase an equivalent amount of goods from Italy in return. Furthermore, Italy's coal purchases from Britain have decreased sharply in the past six months, while coal purchases from Germany have increased significantly. As for oil, large quantities have been purchased and stored, and it is hoped that supplies will continue to be provided by the United States. Timber can be supplied by Austria. If Italy refuses to purchase meat from the Soviet Union, Argentina, and Yugoslavia due to their participation in sanctions, it will turn to Brazil for purchases, as Brazil is not a member of the League of Nations. (Havas Dispatch, 29th)

Naples The steamship "Neptune" sailed from here to Africa yesterday, carrying 400 sanitation and military personnel. Today, the "Sibiania Mano" and "Embria" set sail for Africa, the former carrying 157 officers and 2,267 Blackshirts, and the latter carrying 300 Blackshirts. In addition, the "Adeno" sailed from Salerno City, carrying 68 officers and 580 Blackshirts. Furthermore, the "Saturn" will sail on November 3rd, carrying 203 officers and 4,200 Blackshirts.

Algerian Merchants Patriotic; Raise Funds to Donate to the Government for Troop Support 43

Algiers Many Algerian merchants, mostly Muslims, have raised 600,000 French francs in silver coins, many mules and horses, and other wealth to donate to the authorities for troop support. Some have also donated land and real estate. The authorities have decided to hold a grand ceremony tomorrow to accept the property donated by the people. (Havas Dispatch, 29th)

Italian Aircraft Reconnoiter Magal; Italian Troops on the Northern Route Have Entered Waterlogged Terrain 44

(London) Although the Ethiopian army is avoiding a major decisive battle with the Italian army on the Wolkayte front, it appears that Magal will be the site of the first major battle since the outbreak of war between Italy and Ethiopia. Italian aircraft have reconnoitered the city today and discovered that a strong Ethiopian army is stationed there. The exact number is unknown, but it is believed that they are numerous. Aircraft opened fire to assist, intending to defend against the Italian army there.

According to a report from the Italian army in Eritrean Ili'itri, the Italian army on the northern route began its advance on October 26th and has now occupied the land between the Tekeze River and the Merara River tributaries. The Second Army Corps has advanced to the Fefe watershed, a tributary of the Tekeze River. The outposts are often heavily sniped at night by the Ethiopian army, but there has been no fierce resistance so far. After three days of attack, the Italian army on the northern route has entered waterlogged terrain, so the military strategy is now more convenient than before. At the same time, the area southwest of Eritrean Ili'itri, bounded by the Setit River, is little known. The battle has been ongoing for a month. The area is hot and humid, with marshes and plantations interspersed. There are also many wild animals. The Italian army denies that the river army has invaded Eritrean Ili'itri, saying that the Italian side is defending a 50-mile-long river with very few soldiers, resisting several Ethiopian teams, each with about 500 soldiers. The Italian army ambushes the riverbank with machine guns, opening fire when Ethiopians attempt to drive cattle and sheep to the water. (Reuters Dispatch, 30th)

Roosevelt Reaffirms Peace Advocacy; Designates Armistice Day as a Holiday 45

(Washington) President Roosevelt recently issued an order designating November 11th, Armistice Day, as an official holiday in the United States. He also issued an official statement, stating: "We should use this memorial day to express our determination to maintain friendly relations with all nations and to believe that permanent peace should and can be achieved everywhere in the world." Dike of the Chezhou River in Guanyun Collapses 46

(Xuzhou) The north dike of the Chezhou River in Yilu Township, Guanyun County, collapsed again yesterday due to the impact of salt ice. The breach is more than 20 zhang wide, and the torrent is flowing fiercely, heading straight for the Longyu Dang area east of Mount Fu. Except for a small portion south of Zousi Gully, the western dike has been completely destroyed. All of the villages that had not yet been flooded, including Mahao Village, Zhuangjia Village, Zheng Village, Lu Village, and Hexing Village, spanning dozens of li, have been submerged. The newly built dike from Da Yishan to Da Chai Shu section west of Jiankeyi has suffered considerable collapse due to the scouring of the water. (Central News Agency Dispatch, 30th)

Key Points of the Trademark Law Amendment 60

(Nanjing) The Trademark Law Amendment to be reviewed by the Legislative Yuan on the 31st will amend Articles 1, 3, 14, 27, 28, and 40 of the current law, and delete Article 4. The key points of the amendment are: (1) The wording used in trademarks includes pronunciation; (2) When two or more persons apply separately for registration of the same or similar trademark for the same commodity, the one who actually used it first in China and without interruption should be allowed to register; (3) If a trademark is altered or has annotations added and is used in a way that implies something else, the Trademark Office may, in its official capacity or upon the application of a party with vested interests, revoke it. (Central News Agency Dispatch, 30th)

The Sale of National Ships to Foreign Merchants Requires Cancellation of Registration with the Navigation Administration 62

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Communications replied to the Shanghai Navigation Administration that if national ships are sold to foreign merchants, the original owner should be required to apply for cancellation of registration in accordance with Article 46 of the Ship Registration Law, without any restrictions. Furthermore, ship mortgages and leases should be registered in accordance with the law. Even if one party obtaining the mortgage right or lease right is a foreign national, the ship itself is still subject to the laws of China before losing its Chinese nationality, so they should be required to apply for registration in accordance with the law. As for navigation fees, they should be handled in accordance with the regulations on ships operating in waterways. (Special Dispatch, 30th)

Soviet Scientists' Research Reveals Tea Contains Vitamins; Can Prevent Anemia 83

(TASS, Vladivostok, October 6) Kornytsky, of the Far Eastern Branch of the Blood Transfusion Institute, discovered that ordinary tea contains a large amount of Vitamin C. One gram of dried tea contains 4 to 6 milligrams of Vitamin C. Drinking 3 to 5 grams of tea per day can prevent anemia, and drinking 6 to 10 grams of tea per day can cure anemia. Kornytsky's discovery is of great interest in theory, because Vitamin C is easily destroyed by oxygen in the air, so it almost completely disappears in dried vegetables and dried fruits. Kornytsky pointed out that dry tea contains concentrated Vitamin C due to certain chemical characteristics of dry tea leaves that contain certain enzymes. Experiments have proven that the way tea preserves vitamins can be artificially manufactured and used for other plants containing vitamins. This makes the manufacturing of anti-anemia foods and the preservation of vitamins in dried fruits and vegetables easier to implement. This discovery is of great benefit because it can meet the sorely felt need for foods rich in Vitamin C.

The Course of the Italian Occupation of Adowa and Future Difficulties After the Start of the War Against Abyssinia 85

— Roman Correspondence

The war between Italy and Abyssinia began "unofficially" on October 2nd. The so-called unofficial start is another way of saying "undeclared war." In fact, the two sides have already engaged in artillery fire and hand-to-hand combat. In order to cater to the general oral advocacy of those who oppose war, the word "war" is abandoned and not mentioned, thereby avoiding bearing the legal responsibility for engaging in war. On the afternoon of the 2nd, Italy held a national general mobilization exercise. On the same day, it "resisted" Abyssinia in Africa, held a large-scale bombing in the skies over the black empire, and the army advanced on multiple routes at the same time. From then on, the disaster of war began. On the fourth day after the start of the war, Italy occupied Adowa in Abyssinia. The land is located in the northwestern part of Abyssinia and is close to Italian-owned Eritrea. Forty years ago (March 1, 1896), the Italian army lost contact between its left and right wings and was defeated here by Abyssinia. As a result, a treaty of peace was signed, promising Abyssinia's independence (before this, Abyssinia was an Italian protectorate). This was certainly a disgrace in the eyes of the Italians, and the Fascist Party government, which prides itself on restoring the glory of the ancient Roman Empire, sought to reoccupy the area as soon as possible to vent its accumulated resentment. On the day of the occupation (the 6th of this month), which was a Sunday, all newspapers suspended publication. The central party department also widely printed and posted in the streets Propaganda Department Bulletin No. 14 (in modern Italian history, this bulletin has become an immortal document). For a time, slogans and catchphrases such as "Adowa is ours!" could be seen everywhere. Crowds gathered in groups, parading in the streets, shouting slogans, and two-color national flags were hung in every household in the city to celebrate the victory. In the evening, even more crowds held torches and demonstrated everywhere, the most lively of which was the Venice Square in front of the Tomb of the Unknown Soldier. The Italian people are originally sanguine, passionate and romantic, and have a strong sense of patriotism. This time, the reoccupation of Adowa eliminated the shame of forty years in one day and was the first victory in the advance into Abyssinia. No wonder the public celebrated like crazy.

That Abyssinia lost a city after only three or four days of fighting between the two sides was indeed due to the strength of Italy's military power, but whether Abyssinia had put up a fierce resistance is a question that everyone is jointly doubting and exploring. Regarding the fall of Adowa, there are two theories: one is that Italy first carried out heavy bombing with its fierce air force, and then the army advanced in total, but still encountered a counterattack from Abyssinian convoys. Soldiers on both sides engaged in hand-to-hand combat with short swords and bayonets, resulting in serious casualties (700 Italian deaths and more than 1,300 Abyssinian deaths). The British Times has described it as Hand-to-hand Battle. The other theory is that although Adowa is a large city on the northwestern border of Abyssinia, it is not a key location. It is quite far from the Abyssinian capital Addis Ababa. The Abyssinian king knew that the Italian army had been defeated in that area in the past, and this time it would spare no sacrifice to reoccupy it. Instead of greatly damaging its military strength for this one city, it would be better to preserve its vitality and plan for the main battle in the interior. Therefore, abandoning Adowa may have been a predetermined military plan of Abyssinia. In any case, Italy has finally occupied this city, and it is also a good propaganda tool to encourage the public, inspire the army, and continue to advance. In terms of the matter itself, it is indeed a great victory, and it is almost undeniable. What is concerning is that although the occupation of Adowa is a major victory (and the advance has continued in recent days, and almost the entire Tigray region of Abyssinia has been occupied by the Italian army), the difficulties encountered after this victory and the difficulty in dealing with them will increase day by day.

From a military point of view, regardless of which of the above two theories is true, it is generally recognized that Abyssinia fiercely resisted the Italian army. In terms of weapons, Italy has airplanes, cannons, and all the latest scientific killing tools. When necessary, it may even have military equipment that is more potent than dumdum bullets and poison gas. Abyssinia has no possibility of comparison and resistance on this point. However, Abyssinia is mountainous, the African climate is unfavorable to airplanes and ordinary soldiers, and the situation is not to be taken lightly. Its people are fierce, brave, and good at fighting. Although the Italians are enthusiastic, when faced with them, they will also be difficult enemies to deal with. However, modern warfare is not only a struggle of physical strength but also a struggle of intelligence and scientific tools. On this point, it is Abyssinia's greatest weakness. Forty years ago, Abyssinia may have been able to subdue the Italian army temporarily, but in today's era, forty years later, Italy's progress is enough to overcome Abyssinia dozens of times over. Abyssinia has no air force strength to speak of (it is said that there are only six airplanes, two of which cannot even fight), which is not enough to withstand a single blow from Italy. Even in terms of the army, although the Italian army does not have deep war experience (most of those fighting in Africa this time are young people around the age of twenty. Although veterans of the last war have voluntarily requested to participate and have been promised by Mussolini to be allowed to organize a "Typha Division," they have not yet set out), they are specially trained on weekdays, and their discipline and combat power are top-notch. They are also motivated by patriotic emotions, brave and good at fighting, which Abyssinia may not be able to resist.

Therefore, based on this situation, what can be speculated is that if no other forces come out to obstruct and only allow the Italian and Abyssinian sides to fight against each other, then the Italian army's occupation of the Abyssinian capital Addis Ababa may also be possible in a short period of time. However, whether the Geneva side (in fact, the League of Nations is currently controlled by Britain, that is, the British side) can allow the Italian army to continue to advance so aggressively is still an unknown number. Today, our newspaper reporter went out to buy the British Times and the Daily Mail, etc., searching from Venice Square to the Clonei Square in front of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and the railway station, etc., but could not find them anywhere. When asked, the newspaper vendors said that they had not arrived today or that they had already been sold out. Later, after passing by a British friend's place, I learned that after the League of Nations Administrative Council's decision on the 8th that Italy had violated the covenant, the British newspaper's criticism may be valued by the Italians, or it may not be what the Italians want to make public to the masses. For the past two days, the League of Nations General Assembly has begun to discuss the issue of economic sanctions against Italy. If this proposal can be implemented, given Italy's current lack of raw materials and poor financial situation, Italy will indeed feel great pain. However, no matter how diplomatic circumstances develop, Mussolini is determined to move forward. It can be asserted that (sent late on October 10)

Qingdao: Fisheries and Salt Experimental Zone; Ministries of Finance and Industry Assign Personnel to Organize Experiment; Term Tentatively Set at Two Years 86

Qingdao Correspondence: In order to test and promote the implementation of measures for changing and manufacturing fishing salt, the Ministries of Finance and Industry have designated Qingdao as the Fisheries and Salt Experimental Zone. In May of this year, the two ministries appointed Chen Tiancai and Hou Zhaohai as preparation committee members, and Chen Houzai and Zhang Naigao as investigators, to carry out preparation and investigation matters. Recently, the preparations have been completed, and the Ministries of Finance and Industry have jointly appointed Chu Bo (Director of the Qingdao Municipal Social Affairs Bureau), Hou Zhaohai (Technician of the Ministry of Industry), and Wu Shiyao (Director of the Qingdao Salt Affairs Inspection Office) as committee members, and issued the organizational charter and committee seal of the zone. The committee held its first meeting in Qingdao on the 29th. First, Hou Zhaohai reported on the progress of the preparations, followed by the adoption of (1) immediately putting the seal into use and submitting it to the ministries for record, and informing relevant agencies by letter, (2) deciding to appoint eleven technicians, clerks, and employees, (3) establishing an office at 73 Taiping Road, Qingdao, etc. As for the determination of the implementation plan and the procurement of various equipment, etc., they will be discussed further after the technical conference has made a decision. The charter of the experimental zone is appended below:

Organizational Charter of the Qingdao Fisheries and Salt Experimental Zone of the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Industry, Article 1: In order to test and promote the implementation of measures for changing and manufacturing fishing salt, the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Industry designate Qingdao as the Fisheries and Salt Experimental Zone. Article 2: A committee shall be established in this experimental zone to preside over the experimental matters in this zone, which shall be organized by the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Industry by appointing the following personnel: (1) One representative each from the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Industry, (2) One local fishery supervisor. Article 3: The responsibilities of the committee are as follows: (1) Matters relating to fishing salt experimentation and research, (2) Matters relating to the guidance of local salt affairs agencies in the preparation and distribution of fishing salt, (3) Matters relating to the research on the improvement of fishing salt transportation and sales, (4) Matters relating to the investigation of the salt usage of fishermen, (5) Other experimental matters. Article 4: The committee may appoint four technicians and three clerks, and shall report to the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Industry for record after the appointment. Article 5: The committee may employ employees as appropriate for writing documents. Article 6: The committee shall submit the work progress and an overview of received documents to the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Industry for verification on a monthly basis. Article 7: The experimental period is tentatively set for two years. Article 8: Detailed rules for the operation of the committee shall be determined separately.

Wuxi: Money Shop Runner Flees with Embezzled Funds 90

Zhang Xichen, a runner at the Ruichangrun Money Shop (managed by Wu Buzhou) in Jiangyin Lane, Wuxi, is from Jiangyin, in his early twenties. He has always been quite loyal to his duties. Recently, Zhang personally failed in trading soybeans and other goods on the exchange, suffering heavy losses. He had previously borrowed 1,000 yuan from Dr. Tan Shumo as capital, resulting in his inability to repay the debt. Desperate, Zhang falsely claimed on the morning of the day before yesterday that he needed to return to Cheng for a trip. He then obtained 3,000 yuan in outstanding funds for circulation from the Fuyuan Money Shop and a cash draft of 3,000 yuan from the Fuyu Money Shop (according to this silver draft, there were no proper procedures or evidence, relying entirely on the credit of the runners, but it had to be cleared on the same day). He then used 1,000 yuan to repay the debt to Tan, and fled with the remaining 5,000 yuan, disappearing without a trace. It was not until around 6:00 PM, when Fuyu sought to recover the 3,000 yuan silver draft, that the theft was discovered. Detectives were sent out, but there was no trace of him. With the 3,000 yuan at stake, Fuyu Zhuang requested the Money Industry Association to convene a meeting of the trade at around 7:00 PM. The result of the discussion was that the Ruichangrun Money Shop would find Zhang within a week before further action would be considered.

Letter to the Editor

Respected Editor,

Your newspaper's local correspondence on the 27th of this month reported that the former Magistrate of Jingjiang, Li Jinfang, had personnel remaining in the county to handle handover matters who refused to cooperate, and also stated that the magistrate had privately deposited tax funds to earn interest, that the malfeasance had been discovered, and that the personnel remaining in the county were being held under guard by the county government, etc. On the day the report appeared, Jinfang happened to be in the provincial capital, and inquiries with the government office and other departments revealed that no order had been issued to have the newly appointed officials guard the personnel handling the handover matters. The handover had already been completed, and he had already left Jingjiang for Wuxi. Furthermore, since the establishment of the new accounting system in Jiangsu, all taxes have been registered daily by an accounting director dispatched by the Finance Department, and current funds are all deposited in the Jiangsu Farmers' Bank, which acts as the agent treasury. All interest earned is listed as legitimate government revenue. The idea of a county magistrate privately depositing tax funds to earn interest is, under the Jiangsu system, simply impossible in any county. Therefore, it is unnecessary for Jinfang alone to expend effort in self-defense. We respectfully request that you publish this letter of correction to inform those who are unaware.

Sincerely,

Li Pufang, Former Magistrate of Jingjiang

October 29th,

To the Editorial Department of Shen Bao

Today is the Difficult End of October: Banks and Money Shops are Busy Settling Accounts; Commercial and Industrial Enterprises Expected to Weather the Storm 94

The long-term credit extended by banks and money shops is due at the end of October. To support commerce and industry, special accommodations are being made for maturing long-term loans, with interest settlement extended to the end of April. However, both banks and money shops are particularly busy settling accounts. Yesterday, the exchange rate for silver dollars in the money market was 1.70 yuan in both the morning and afternoon sessions, an increase of 0.02 yuan from the previous day. However, the "jiatou jia shui" (premium on silver coins), suddenly surged to a peak of 0.70 yuan yesterday, a significant increase of 0.50 yuan from the previous day, the highest since the end of April. This is because the sudden increase in money shops' remittances to banks caused an imbalance between supply and demand.

Extension of Interest Settlement Fully Completed: Long-term credit loans extended by Shanghai banks, money shops, and Ningbo-Hankou money shops in Shanghai are all due today. Although commercial and industrial enterprises that borrowed had already contacted banks and money shops to negotiate interest settlement and extensions until the end of April, both industries made special accommodations to support commerce and industry, and most of the extension procedures have been completed. However, several more were completed yesterday. As for new long-term loans, they are much lower than last year, but by last night, everything had been fully completed.

All Industries Safely Passed Yesterday: Although the difficulty of the end of October is not as great as when closing the books for the year, it is similar to the end of April. Fortunately, after the Ministry of Finance provided relief to the money shops and the banks and money shops cooperated fully, no unfortunate incidents occurred. As for the long-term credit of commercial and industrial enterprises, thanks to the banks and money shops agreeing to extensions and the commodity loan relief provided by the Industrial and Commercial Loan Committee, no major factories, firms, or companies were forced to suspend operations yesterday due to a lack of funds. As for the closure of businesses like Yongda Shoe Store on Guangdong Road, they were unrelated to the end of October.

Shipping Companies Request the Issuance of Public Bonds; Rejected Three Times by the Ministry; Approval to Waive Tonnage Dues for Suspended Vessels, but Not to Abolish the School Surtax; Shipping Companies Hope for the Early Announcement of a Reorganization Plan 95

According to the Xin Sheng She, the Shanghai Shipping Industry Association's request to issue shipping industry public bonds and abolish the 30% surtax on tonnage dues have both been rejected. Shipping companies are in extreme decline, with as many as 40 vessels suspended. They hope for the early announcement of a reorganization plan to relieve the shipping crisis. Details are as follows:

Shipping Industry Public Bonds Rejected Three Times

Shipping companies submitted a request to the Ministry of Communications in 1930 to issue 10 million yuan in shipping industry public bonds, but it has never been realized. In July of this year, the Shipping Industry Association, recognizing the increasingly severe decline of the shipping industry, the financial constraints, and the difficulty of maintaining operations, had no choice but to resubmit the old proposal, appealing to the government to quickly issue public bonds to provide relief. After deliberation by the Ministries of Finance and Communications, it was rejected twice due to the lack of a guaranteed fund. The Shipping Industry Association submitted a third request, proposing to designate the surplus tonnage dues as the fund and again requesting approval for the issuance. The Ministry of Communications has again issued a rejection, stating that the tonnage dues have already been incorporated into the national budget and the request cannot be approved, and instructing all shipping companies to be informed.

Exemption from Tonnage Dues for Suspended Vessels Approved

The Shipping Industry Association, due to vessels being suspended without business and therefore having no income, had requested the Jianghai Customs Tax Affairs Department and the Finance Ministry Customs Administration to approve an exemption from tonnage dues, which has been approved. Recognizing that they have been paying a 30% tonnage duty surtax for naval academy funding for six years and the accumulated amount is substantial, and that the shipping industry is now in decline and in dire straits, unable to even sustain itself, they specifically requested the Ministry of Communications to approve a suspension of the levy, which has been rejected.

Hoping for the Announcement of the Reorganization Plan

The decline of the shipping industry has reached an extreme point. As many as 40 vessels are docked in the Huangpu River without cargo to load. The shipping companies' requests to issue public bonds and suspend the 30% surtax on tonnage dues have both been rejected. Their only hope at present is for the Ministry of Communications to quickly announce the proposed reorganization plan for national shipping administration, so that vessels that have been suspended without funds to operate, such as the Daxing Company's Daxing and Hongxing vessels, can resume operations. Various shipping companies have inquired with the industry association, asking them to forward inquiries to the Ministry of Communications.

Successful Pledge of Telegraph and Postal Administration Bonds; Contract Negotiations Commence; China Communications Bank and Other Banks to Undertake the Loan and Form a Syndicate to Handle a Total of 6 Million Yuan with Interest Around 8 Percent 96

After the Ministry of Communications issued 10 million yuan in Telegraph and Postal Administration bonds, it dispatched Section Chief Zhou Youduan to jointly consult with Post Office Remittance Bureau Director Shen Shuyu and Deputy Director Zhou Shouliang, and various banks, regarding pledge matters. The specific methods have been agreed upon, and contract negotiations commenced yesterday. Details are as follows:

Methods Agreed Upon: The Telegraph and Postal Administration Bonds are being pledged to Shanghai banks. Shen Shuyu, Zhou Shouliang, and Zhou Youduan consulted with managers from various banks, such as Song Hanzhang, Tang Shoumin, Hu Bijang, Ye Fuxiao, Chen Zheqing, Song Ziliang, Qu Jigang, Wang Boyuan, Chen Guangfu, Wu Yunzhai, etc. on the concrete measures. The specific methods have been agreed upon. The lending banks are Central Bank, Bank of China, Bank of Communications, Shanghai Bank, Jincheng Bank, Continental Bank, China & South Sea Bank, Yien Yieh Commercial Bank, Zhejiang Industrial Bank, China Products Bank, Guohua Commercial Bank, and Ken Yieh Bank. The Ministry of Communications plans to pledge 6 million yuan. The amount committed by each bank has not yet been fully decided, but it is generally expected to be sufficient.

Contract Negotiations: A Xin Sheng She reporter visited Ministry of Communications Section Chief Zhou Youduan last night. According to him, the matters concerning the pledge of the Telegraph and Postal Administration Bonds have been largely settled, thanks to Director Shen and Deputy Director Zhou consulting with various banks. The number of subscriptions by the various banks still needs to be finalized. It is expected that banks in Shanghai, such as the Central Bank, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications, will all participate in the subscription. The contract has begun to be negotiated and is expected to be formally signed soon. The terms and interest rates will be announced after the contract is signed.

Forming a Syndicate: The lending banks, such as the Bank of China and the Bank of Communications, will form a syndicate to manage the loan after the amount of each bank's commitment has been decided. The total loan amount may reach 6 million yuan. The bonds are secured by international telegraph revenue, making them very reliable. The loan proceeds will be used entirely for the development of telegraph administration. The term of the loan has been rumored to be seven years, but this is not confirmed. The interest rate is approximately 8 percent. In this time of tight credit and economic depression, the success of this loan is no easy feat.

Wang Qingmu Discusses Diverting the Yellow River; Letter to Chairman Chen of Jiangsu States that Water Management Should Be Conducted Underground 100

Mr. Wang Dankui, a respected elder of this province, has been concerned about water conservancy issues. Recently, he has repeatedly expressed his views on the Yellow River management problem. He recently sent a letter to Chairman Chen Guofu of Jiangsu Province, discussing the merits and demerits of diverting the Yellow River water in northern Jiangsu. The following is an excerpt from the original letter: "The Yellow River flows south, and northern Jiangsu has suffered severe disasters. Once it reaches the territory of Haishu, it is essential to ensure smooth discharge. Recently, reports stated that the channel of the Burning Incense River, which is the mouth of the river, is still slowly draining, despite being dredged. Further, reports from Xuzhou stated that two river mouths of the Burning Incense River in the eastern irrigation districts have been widened to ten zhang and deepened to six chi. According to the above two reports, the dredging of the Burning Incense River has only reached a depth of six chi, and the portion outside of the mouth cannot be improved by human effort, and the silting up condition is easily imagined. Last year, the opening of the Liu Tang estuary also did not consider the interior and exterior of the river mouth, so it also lacks smooth discharge, similar to the Burning Incense River. These coastal river mouths are shallow. There might be blocking sandbars. It is not possible to have a smooth inner flow into the sea without dredging by machine ship. Furthermore, there are two tides every twenty-four hours. The incoming tide takes about ten hours and the outgoing tide about fourteen hours. When the tide comes in, the river water is stopped by the tide and the silting beneath, which becomes a backflow. Every day, there will be ten hours when the river water cannot flow out. If the river mouth interior and exterior are dredged to at least twelve chi deep, the deeper the better, the water will flow smoothly during low tide. Even at high tide, the upper level will still be pushed and the lower level will not be silted, but there will be pressure, which will drive the water out faster. Water can flow smoothly for twenty-four hours and it would be different from the current sluggish situation. All of the sea estuaries should be deeply dredged and the Huai River outlet opened up at the Taizikou. Then all of the flooding in Su Lu area can be gone without waiting for the completion of the Huai River plan. Dredging the machine ship in Shanghai's Dredging Bureau has proven to be effective. It should request the central authority to borrow and all the costs should be considered as proper spending by the Dredging Fund and reimbursed accordingly. Guiding the Huai River and dredging should assist each other. Regarding the silt conditions of the estuaries, the Maritime Survey Bureau should investigate and draw charts for use. More over, water should be guided underground and should not cause harm but be helpful. Yu the Great diverted the water to the sea. Now, tens of thousands of people are working on the Guiding the Huai project. Yu also used the method of water flowing through large rivers. The Book of History mentioned dredging the fields, and the Analects mentioned trying to dredge the ditches. The ditches are water channels on the farmland. Yu made plans for the people to work on it. Therefore, there were small rivers aside from the sea that water can go to, but not entirely the sea. The Yellow River now goes south and flows on the ground and defenses are built on the ground. In western Lu and northern Su, the ditches have not been restored for a long time. If it is flooded, it will be water everywhere and if it is dry, the ground will be red. When managing water, we should start with the ancient books. The ditches should follow the intent, but not the exact method. We should dredge the ditches to fit local conditions and make the small rivers flow underground. The authorities must do this. For the unflooded areas, we should plan and dredge so that the water can run into the small rivers, and when the flooded area retreats, we should dredge the ground to let people understand the value of water. Wang Qingmu, October 20, year 24."

Registered Opium Smokers to Reach 20,000; Voluntary Registration Ends Today; Compulsory Self-Reporting for Amnesty Still Under Consideration; Temporary Opium Addiction Treatment Hospital to Start Preparations Immediately; Compulsory Registration Starts Tomorrow 107

New Voice News Agency reports: Opium smoker registration in this city, which started on July 1st and was extended to today as the deadline, has seen a total of 18,199 registrations. Compulsory registration will begin tomorrow, with the implementation of arrests and fines for opium offenders. Details are as follows:

Registered Opium Smokers to Reach 20,000 108

Since the Public Safety Bureau (PSB) began opium smoker registration on July 1st, a total of 18,199 opium smokers have registered as of yesterday. Among them, 6,888 have obtained ordinary addiction treatment licenses, 8,479 have obtained licenses for the impoverished, totaling 15,167 license holders. 1,384 are undergoing addiction treatment, and 1,448 have registered for treatment but have not yet been sent to hospitals. In total, 18,199 opium smokers have registered. The PSB conducted a total of three investigations into opium smokers in this city. All opium smokers found were registered, achieving excellent results. The three opium smoker investigations are scheduled to end today. It is estimated that the number of registered opium smokers will increase by 2,000 to 3,000 today, quickly bringing the total number of registered opium smokers to around 20,000.

Self-Reporting for Amnesty Under Serious Consideration 109

The PSB will cease voluntary opium smoker registration from tomorrow and will begin arresting opium offenders, imposing fines ranging from 50 to 300 yuan, and sending them to addiction treatment hospitals for compulsory detoxification. All PSB branch bureaus and teams are required to submit arrest reports to the bureau within three hours of detaining opium smokers. Any unauthorized punishment or delayed submission will be severely punished without leniency upon investigation. However, the PSB recognizes that the city is vast, and it was inevitable that some opium smokers would be missed during the voluntary registration period. Whether to grant amnesty from fines to opium smokers who self-report during the compulsory registration period is currently under serious consideration, but a decision will be made within days.

Opium Addiction Treatment Hospital to Start Preparations Immediately 110

The PSB anticipates that during the compulsory registration period, the number of arrested opium offenders who cannot afford to pay fines or obtain licenses will be high, and they will have to be sent to the city's addiction treatment hospitals for compulsory detoxification. However, the city's addiction treatment hospitals can only accommodate a maximum of 20 to 30 people per day. If this number is exceeded, the hospitals in both the Shanghai South and Shanghai North districts will not be able to accommodate them immediately. The PSB detention center can only hold a maximum of 300 opium offenders, and if the number increases, it will be impossible to detain them. Therefore, a request was submitted to the municipal government to order the Health Bureau to prepare a temporary addiction treatment hospital with a capacity of 500 people to accommodate the opium offenders undergoing compulsory detoxification during the compulsory registration period. Yesterday, the bureau received a reply from the municipal government, ordering the bureau to jointly prepare the establishment of this temporary addiction treatment hospital with the Health Bureau immediately. Before the addiction treatment hospital is established, the PSB will consult with the local court to temporarily borrow a portion of the Caohejing Prison to house the opium offenders temporarily detained by the PSB. Once the addiction treatment hospital has available rooms and beds, they will be transferred separately for treatment. The PSB also noted that the food expenses for all temporarily detained prisoners are considerable. The previously approved monthly food budget of 300 yuan is insufficient. Therefore, the bureau has submitted a request to the municipal government for approval to allow actual reporting and reimbursement of expenses during the compulsory registration period, without being restricted by the original budget.

Rewards for Reporting Private Opium Use; Fines Used as Incentives 111

The PSB also announced that during the compulsory registration period, to encourage citizens to report unlicensed opium smokers, in accordance with Article 4 of the "Measures for Handling Registration of Opium Smoking Households within a Time Limit," 30% of the fines will be awarded to informants. Those who make false accusations will be punished according to the law. The bureau is currently drafting measures for the registration, reward, and punishment of informants.

Transfer of Cadres and Police to Assist in Security and Guard Duties 112

During the compulsory registration period, there will be many opium offenders and procedures will be particularly cumbersome. The procedures for opium smokers undergoing addiction treatment or obtaining licenses for the impoverished, including finding guarantors and verifying guarantor information, will be particularly complicated. The current number of police officers is insufficient to handle the workload. Therefore, the PSB has temporarily transferred two squads of police officers from the Police Headquarters to assist in security and guard duties.

Working Day and Night to Handle Opium Cases 113

After completing the opium smoker registration procedures, filling out the application form, and paying the license fee, the PSB will first issue a temporary receipt and then issue the official license at a later date. Therefore, there is a significant time difference between the registration and the issuance of the license. During the voluntary registration period, opium smokers applied for addiction treatment licenses voluntarily, so a slight delay in the issuance date was not a problem. However, starting in November, all opium smokers who are caught will be subject to compulsory registration. If a temporary receipt is issued first and then the license is issued at a later date, the procedure will be overly complicated, and after a certain period of time, many opium smokers will hide or flee, and many addiction treatment licenses will not be delivered. Therefore, the PSB will change its approach during the compulsory registration period, registering and issuing licenses simultaneously. Opium offenders will be released after obtaining their addiction treatment licenses. The PSB will assign several officials to handle the registration and license issuance procedures for interrogated opium offenders to avoid backlog and streamline the process. The PSB will handle all opium cases sent by the branch bureaus day and night during the first month of compulsory registration, regardless of the time of day.

Progress of the New People's Assistance Society 114

The Salvation Army, as disciples of Christ, practices Christ's great way of saving the world, regardless of international borders or ethnicity. Its purpose is universal love and benevolence, and its spirit is practical action. It originated in England and has spread throughout the world. It has been in China for over a decade and in Shanghai for three years. It has established a Salvation Army headquarters in Beiping and a New People's Assistance Society in Ward Road, Public Concession of Shanghai, specifically to provide assistance to prisoners who have completed their sentences. Those without clothes are provided with clothing, those without lodging are provided with temporary food and accommodation, those without the means to return home are provided with travel expenses or tickets, and those with illnesses are sent to hospitals for free treatment. Various charitable activities are too numerous to mention. To promote the progress of the New People's Assistance Society's work, a branch was established on Kangti Road, French Concession. At the same time, Mr. Hu Dunchu, a master's graduate from the United States, was appointed as the general manager to oversee the society's affairs. Mr. Hu is a devout Christian apostle with a solid foundation in both Chinese and Western literature. After returning from the United States, he served in various business and academic circles for many years and also worked as a certified public accountant and obtained a lawyer's license. He is particularly actively engaged in the work of the New People's Assistance Society branch, sparing no effort. A factory has now been established within the society, employing technicians to teach general young ex-offenders who have no skills, hoping that they will succeed and become self-reliant. Overall, the Salvation Army's various works are truly seeking to transform society and increase the happiness of the nation.

Customs Ordered to Revise Regulations Regarding Navigation of Civil Vessels 118

Tang Haian, Customs Superintendent, and Ba Runsen, Customs Commissioner, issued Notification No. 1473 yesterday, stating that they were ordered to revise the regulations regarding the management of navigation of civil vessels and the limitation of capacity. The notification stated: "We have received an order from the Ministry of Finance stating that the first, second, sixth, seventh, and twelfth articles of the Regulations for the Management of Navigation of Civil Vessels by Customs, as well as the attachments, regarding the limit of 120 metric tons of deadweight, are inconsistent with the provisions of the Maritime Law and should be amended to a maximum capacity of 200 tons. This shall be promulgated and made known to all." Therefore, we must comply with and implement this order. Let all civil vessel navigators and merchants be fully aware of this notification. This notification is hereby issued.
