Ministry of Industry to Build New Fish Market; Opening in Mid-December; All Engineering Completed Long Ago; Fish Merchants' Opposition Resolved 119

The Ministry of Industry, in order to revitalize China's fishing industry, has specially planned to build a large-scale fish market north of Dinghai Bridge in Yangshupu, covering an area of over 50 mu, with a capital of 1 million yuan in national currency. All engineering projects have been completed one after another, and the internal equipment is now being painstakingly arranged. It is expected to formally open in mid-December. At that time, Minister of Industry Chen Gongbo will personally come to Shanghai to preside over the opening. Details are as follows:

Main Structures 120

The main structures of the market are divided into: A. An office building with seven floors. Floors two to four will house the technology room, library, board room, conference room, aquatic product exhibition room, dining hall, and staff bedrooms. Floors five to seven will have a radio room, meteorological observation station, and meteorological signal station. B. A sales floor, covering an area of 6,323 square feet. C. Temporary warehouses, totaling six, each 42 feet long, 25 feet wide, and 14 feet high. D. Floating docks, totaling three, connected by iron chains, with a total length of 600 feet, capable of simultaneously docking two trawlers, two hand-operated net boats, and 24 live fish boats. E. Broker offices, totaling 28 offices. F. A cold storage facility with five cold storage rooms, one ice-making room, one freezing room, and one machine room, etc., contracted by the Xin Hengtai Construction Company. Construction began in July of this year, and all engineering projects have been completed one after another.

Cooperative Efforts 121

The market was originally planned to be jointly operated by the government and merchants. However, local fish merchants believed that the establishment of the market was a prelude to the control of the fishing industry, which would affect their own interests and survival. There was a misunderstanding, so they did not join as merchant shareholders. Although it has now been changed to be wholly state-owned by the Ministry of Industry, the position of broker is intended to be filled by fish merchants. The fish merchants also stated that the total amount of loans given to fishermen over the years has reached more than 2.5 million, averaging about 70,000 yuan per household. If they lose their original position and become brokers in the fish market, this "fish loan" will be uncollectible. Furthermore, according to recent statistics, the total annual trade value of Shanghai fish products averages about 20 million yuan. The commission is 8% of the value, according to precedent, with a total annual income of 1.6 million yuan. The fish market stipulates that the commission is only 6% of the value, and the brokers split the commission with the market in a 5:3 ratio. The net commission income of the fish market is about 700,000 yuan per year, and the fish merchants' income is only 480,000 yuan, a reduction of more than three times the original income. The average annual income per household is only 10,000 yuan, so they are unwilling to join as brokers. Although they have been persuaded several times, the two sides still insist. However, the market believes that the situation is irreversible and cannot be ruined because the fish merchants refuse to serve as brokers. It has now been decided to take decisive action and recruit new people to handle the matter. The fish merchants then became alarmed again and expressed their willingness to accept. The market side did not refuse to accept, and other methods will be sought to resolve all of the above difficulties. The market has now prepared the regulations for fisherman loans, fishery regulations, market organizational law, broker rules, etc., and submitted them to the Ministry for approval and publication. The formal opening date will be held in mid-December. Minister of Industry Chen Gongbo is determined to come to Shanghai personally to preside over the opening.

Market Advantages 122

After the market formally opens, its advantages in terms of economics are: (1) It can balance supply and demand according to market needs, avoiding the evils of price surges and falls, and fish owners can avoid being affected by cheap fish; (2) In addition to paying the appropriate commission, other fees can be waived; (3) Centralized operations require fewer personnel and save expenses, and can also avoid the evils of monopolies and manipulation by a few people; (4) It can level market prices, so that fishermen are not affected by the sharp decline in fish prices, and with the support of financial institutions, the economy can circulate. In terms of facilities: (1) There is a 600-foot long embankment, docks, and warehouses, with quick and convenient loading and unloading; (2) The area is large, and there is plenty of open space around, so market transactions are not crowded or noisy; (3) Market facilities are designed by experts, using scientific methods, and special attention is paid to ventilation, light, and washing, so that the market has no fishy smell and is hygienic; (4) There is a 1,500-ton cold storage facility, with a cold storage capacity of 22,000 dan, so that fish can be stored and sold when needed in the market; (5) There are refrigerated trucks and refrigerated ships, which can transport fresh fish to various places at any time to promote consumption; (6) There is a meteorological station and a radio station, which can report the weather and the supply and demand of fish in various places, as well as the news of fish prices, so that practitioners can have a basis for making decisions; (7) There is a purchasing cooperative, and all fishers can become members to enjoy affordable and high-quality fishing gear and ship supplies; (8) It can act as an agent for fishing boat fees, customs declarations, and other matters. In short, the future formal opening will be of great benefit to controlling the fishing industry economy, developing the future of the fishing industry, and reducing the burden on fishermen.

Continued News of the Postal Bureau's Robbery Case; Chen Qiu and Two Others Await Sentencing; Trial for Monk Wukong and Eight Others to Be Continued 125

On the morning of September 9th, the Shanghai Postal Bureau was robbed of over 91,000 yuan in large denomination bills while delivering the funds to the Guojin Remittance Bureau. The escorts, Rui Lin and Yuan Bingshu, were shot and killed by the armed robbers. Another escort, Zhou Yuchen, was also shot and injured. Afterwards, the Detectives of Dixwell Road Police Station arrested several suspects. After the investigation was concluded, those who were not involved were released one after another, while the remaining ten men and women, including the monk Wukong (secular name Ji Rentang) from Jiangbei, were prosecuted by the police station according to law. The First Special District Local Court has repeatedly conducted inquiries and reported on the situation. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Jiang Shuzi opened the court again, summoned witnesses, and ordered the eleven men and women defendants, including the monk Wukong, Qiu Guobin, Li Yisheng, Li Xueshi, Wu Pangui, Zhou Yaoshi (also known as Zhou Ermazi), Dao Sheng, Ji Wenbin, Ji Chen, Chen Qiu, and Ji Chen to be tried. The police lawyer Zhang Shizhu stated that Ji Rentang, also known as the monk Wukong, had confessed to the police station a few days ago, and that the two defendants, Qiu Guobin and Wu Pangui, could prove the circumstances of the confession at the time. However, the detectives sent to Funing to apprehend the wanted criminal had returned empty-handed, saying that the criminal had fled after hearing the news. Detective No. 296 of the Dixwell Road Police Station reported that when they went to Funing to arrest the suspect, the suspect's entire family had already fled. Qiu Guobin and Wu Pangui testified that Ji Rentang confessed to the police station that he had conspired with Liu Xiaojiaozi and six others to rob the postal bureau, and that Ji had admitted that he was the one who carried the bag containing the banknotes. They both heard Ji's confession. Wang Kan of the Postal Bureau testified that when the bandits fired their guns, he was working in the office and saw three shots fired through the window. The bandit who fired the gun looked like Ji Rentang, but his face was slightly fuller. The court then questioned Ji, who said that the confession at the police station was not his true intention. Qiu and Wu both said that there was no torture at the time, but Ji continued to deny it and requested that the judge examine his body. Then Qiu Guobin said that the black long gown that Ji wore when he went to rob the postal bureau was borrowed from him, and now there is a hole in the right side of the gown, which was made by Ji holding a pistol and firing it from inside the gown.

The Hole Was Made by a Bullet

The court then questioned the defendant Chen Qiu, who testified that Qiu Guobin was her younger brother. The detectives searched her and found 213 yuan in cash, which was the money she earned from participating in a rotating credit association and the money saved by her husband and son over time, and it was not given to her by Guobin. Guobin also testified that although he received 350 yuan, he had used it to buy gold rings, cloth, and pay off debts, and did not give a single cent to his sister. The defendant Wu Pangui still denied going to Wang Chen's house to participate in the conspiracy to rob the postal bureau with monk Wukong, Liu Xiaojiaozi, etc., saying that he had been a police officer in Shanghai for many years, and how dare he do such an illegal thing, and asked for a thorough investigation. But the defendant Ji Chen insisted that she saw Wu Pangui and Wukong secretly talking in the inner room on the third floor of Wang Chen's house, and she had also seen them gathering in a nearby teahouse once. However, she did not hear what they were talking about because they stopped talking as soon as they saw her. The defendant Zhou Yaoshi also denied going to Wang Chen's house to conspire with Wukong, etc. on the opium bed and dividing 110 yuan of the stolen money after the robbery. However, according to Qiu Guobin, he did see Zhou and Wukong smoking opium in the same bed, and he also heard Wukong confess at the police station that he had given Zhou 150 yuan. Zhou also admitted to receiving the money at the time. The court then questioned Wang Chen, who testified that Zhou had two meetings with Liu Xiaojiaozi, Wukong, etc. at her house. Xiaojiaozi asked him how to proceed with the postal bureau robbery, and Zhou replied that he would wait for Wang to arrive before making a decision. But Zhou still denied all of the above statements.

Stubbornly Denying Everything

Later, the court questioned the defendant Liu Daosheng, who testified that he was framed by Ji Wenbin, who had a grudge against him. He said that he was unemployed and stayed at the home of a man named Liang in Funing to work as a cook. The robbery was planned at Liang's house in the fifth or sixth month of the year. It was not until a man surnamed Chen brought a box of pistols from Jiangbei that he knew that the target was the postal bureau. He asked everyone how they would rob the postal bureau, but they did not tell him their plans afterwards. On the afternoon of August 8th, a man surnamed Wang led them out of Liang's house, and Liu Daosheng went with them. Since then, everyone has not returned. Liang's residence was originally a thatched hut, and after getting the stolen money, they abandoned the thatched hut. Later, he heard a man surnamed Chen from the gang say that Liang received more than 30,000 yuan of the stolen money, but he did not get a single cent. Until October 17th, he suddenly met Liu Daosheng and reported it to the police station. He did not know Wukong, etc. The court verified the confession, and since the investigations of Chen Qiu, Li Yisheng, and Wu Pangui were largely clear, the court ordered a preliminary debate on the accusations against these three people. The police lawyer Zhang Shizhu spoke first, stating that Chen Qiu was a poor woman, so where did she get so much cash, which was obviously the stolen money obtained by her brother, and she should be punished for the crime of

Receiving Stolen Goods

As for Li Yisheng, who was a ship's steward, he embezzled 1,000 yuan of stolen money hidden in the pillow by Wang Chen, so he should be charged with the crime of embezzlement in the course of business. Wu Pangui participated in the bandits' conspiracy and was in fact an instigator of the robbery, and he should be punished according to the law. The court, as Wu did not have a designated lawyer, designated Yang Huchen, the defending lawyer for Chen Qiu, to defend Wu Pangui as well. Li Yisheng was defended by his appointed lawyer, Li Zhongwen. After the arguments were made, Judge Jiang ruled that the sentences for the three defendants would be announced next Wednesday. The trial for monk Wukong and the other eight would be continued next Wednesday afternoon. The police took the eleven men and women back to the detention center separately.

Two Britons Shot in Huaye Building; Elderly Briton Dies En Route to Hospital; Young Man Sent to Hospital for Treatment 126

Huaye Building, located at No. 173, Lane 159, Seymour Road, is an apartment building used by Chinese and foreign middle and upper class people. Because of its quiet location, it is home to many residents. However, at 6:15 last night, several gunshots suddenly rang out from Room 44 on the fourth floor of the building. At that time, the building staff were about to leave work for the day when they suddenly heard the shots. They stopped and ran to investigate. They found that the door to the room was closed but not locked. They pushed it open and were shocked to see a young British man shot and lying on the ground, and an elderly British man holding a handgun lying at the door. Both were still warm to the touch and had gunshot wounds. The two were covered in blood, a gruesome sight that sent chills down one's spine. The building staff did not have time to consider the circumstances and immediately telephoned the police station to send an ambulance to rush the two to Hongen Hospital for treatment. En route, the elderly Briton died. His body was sent to the coroner's office and the British Assessor's Office to investigate the truth.

Hu Renfu Commits Suicide by Drowning; British Consul-General Sends Letter and Belongings 129

Letter: Deceived by Others, Drifting to a Foreign Land

Content: Conscience-Stricken, Ashamed to Live On

On the 10th of this month at 9 PM, the British merchant ship "Lishan" was passing outside Yantai Harbor when a man named Hu Renfu suddenly jumped into the sea and drowned. Rescue attempts were unsuccessful. He left behind a letter and belongings, which the shipowner requested the British Consul-General to forward to the Shanghai Municipal Government, seeking his family members to claim them. It is now learned that the Consul-General's letter and a list of Hu Renfu's belongings are as follows:

British Consul-General's Letter: According to the report of the owner of the British merchant ship "Lishan," a Chinese passenger claiming to be named Hu Renfu jumped overboard at 9:30 PM on October 10th this year, when the ship was 15 English miles outside Yantai Harbor, on its way to Tianjin. This act was witnessed by a Russian shipping police officer on board, who immediately raised an alarm. The ship stopped immediately and launched a lifeboat. Despite a thorough search at sea, no trace of the person was found. Among the items left behind were a watch, four yuan and some cents in banknotes, and a suicide note from Hu Renfu. The note indicated that he committed suicide. Hu Renfu boarded the ship in Yantai, apparently heading to Tianjin. His address is unknown, but his accent suggests he was from Shanghai. The Consul-General is now forwarding his belongings and the letter to your Worship the Mayor, and respectfully requests that your Worship investigate the above circumstances and take appropriate action. Addressed to Shanghai Mayor Wu. From John B. Affleck, British Consul-General in Shanghai, October 21st.

Content of the Suicide Note: Hu's suicide note reads as follows: "I drifted to a foreign land, deceived by others. My conscience reproaches me, and I am ashamed to live on. I hereby take this opportunity to find my final resting place. I deeply apologize to the shop owner. The remaining fifteen yuan and clothing can be used for the cost of a coffin. I would be grateful and thankful if the Public Security Bureau could assist with this matter." Signed, Hu Renfu, night of October 9th.

List of Belongings: The belongings left by Hu included a suitcase, a hat, a watch, a cotton quilt, four books, a sleeveless undershirt, a shirt, a collar, and four yuan and one cent in silver dollars.

Mother and Daughter Both Abducted and Sold; Mother Escapes but Daughter's Whereabouts Unknown; Ma Yongbiao and Others Await Sentencing 130

Zhao Tangshi, a woman from Shaoxing, aged thirty-eight, reported to the Huisi Police Station the night before last that Ma Yongbiao (also known as "Little Shaoxing"), residing at No. 192, North Xizang Road, had tricked and abducted her and her eleven-year-old daughter, Zhao Aju, a month ago, and had them taken to Shandong to be sold. The money was used up. Now, having been rescued, she arrived in Shanghai at noon today. Her daughter's whereabouts are still unknown. She requested an investigation. The police station dispatched Chinese detectives Shen Dehui and Bao Ziduo, who arrested Ma Yongbiao. They also went to No. 87, Lane 302, Haifang Road, West Shanghai, and apprehended an accomplice from Anhui, Geng Huaixin (also known as "Old Man Geng"), and brought them back to the police station for detention. Yesterday morning, they were sent to the Eighth Criminal Division of the First Special Court. Police lawyer Zhang Tianyin filed a public prosecution in accordance with Article 298 of the Criminal Law regarding the crime of abduction. According to the informant Zhao Tangshi, she and the defendant Ma Yongbiao were from the same village and were distantly related. In the eighth month of the lunar calendar this year, she met Ma on Qipu Road. During their conversation, she mentioned that she was looking for an employer as a servant. Ma told her that since the war had broken out in Shanghai, the market was bad and wages were very low. It would be better to go to Shandong as a servant, where men could earn twenty yuan a month and women could earn thirty. She believed him and asked him to recommend her. On the Mid-Autumn Festival, she brought her daughter Aju to Ma's house to stay temporarily. A few days later, the second defendant, Geng Huaixin, arrived, and Ma instructed her to go with Geng. She then went to Shandong with Aju and Geng, staying at the home of Geng's friend, Song Shipan, for about twenty days. It wasn't until September 26th that Geng, Song, and others took her to Zhu Yaozeng's house. At that time, she only knew that she was working as a servant for the Zhu family. Later, without any explanation, she was told that Zhu had bought her for two hundred yuan to be his wife and presented a written agreement. Only then did she wake up as if from a dream. She immediately cried and told Zhu about being deceived and asked for help. Zhu also understood the inside story but did not provide assistance. Zhu issued a letter, entrusting the local Red Cross to arrange for her to be sent back to Shanghai. She arrived in Shanghai yesterday afternoon and reported it to the police station. She learned that her daughter Aju had also been sold in Shandong and did not know where she was. She requested a thorough investigation. Ma Yongbiao confessed that he and Zhao Tangshi were from the same village. After meeting her on the road a month ago, she wanted him to sell her daughter Aju for her. So, he asked Geng Huaixin to take her to Shandong to sell her. He did not know that Zhao Tangshi had also been sold. A few days ago, Geng returned to Shanghai and gave him five yuan, which he had already spent. Geng Huaixin also confessed that he took Zhao Tangshi and her daughter to Shandong. Song Shipan found employers to sell them separately. In total, he sold them for one hundred and thirty yuan. After deducting forty yuan for travel expenses and thirty yuan for food, there were sixty yuan left. He gave Ma thirty-five yuan and only used twenty-five yuan himself. After Magistrate Wu Zehan reviewed the confessions, he ordered Ma and Geng to be detained and await sentencing on the morning of the 31st of this month.

The Chief Inspector of the Public Concession Police summoned the Chinese and foreign chief and deputy detectives from each police station to a special meeting at the Central Patrol Sponsoring Society on Sima Road at 2 PM the day before yesterday (the 29th). Those who agreed were to sign and implement the measure. The managers unanimously agreed to assist in the prohibition of smoking and signed accordingly before dispersing.

Wedding Pranks Uninterrupted for Ten Days; Bride Commits Suicide Due to Stimulation; Stabs Throat with Scissors and Sleeps Under Bed; Found and Sent to Hospital; Life Expected to Be Saved 135

Chen Pinshan, a 19-year-old from Ningbo, the owner of the Xingfa Inn at No. 116, Huoshu Mill Street in the French Concession, whose father has passed away, and the inn is managed by his daughter. Chen, through a matchmaker, engaged Zhang Lanqing (18 years old this year), the daughter of Zhang Zi'an, a fellow villager from the Ningkang Inn on Min'guo Road, Old North Gate, as his wife. The parents of both parties, believing that the man and woman had reached marriageable age, chose an auspicious day, the 20th of this month, to marry Zhang Lanqing at the Hongyun Restaurant Auditorium on Min'guo Road, opposite the New North Gate. After the wedding, they rented a room in the second-floor pavilion at No. 1, New Kang Lane (opposite the back door of Xingfa Inn) on Mill Street. Chen Pinshan was lame in one foot. Because it was the beginning of their marriage, the young couple's love was very deep. However, according to the bad customs of Ningbo, there are wedding pranks when marrying a bride, which are strange and varied. As a new bride, Chen Pinshan could not avoid the secular customs after marriage, so the wedding pranks have continued uninterrupted for ten days, causing the bride Chen Zhang Juqing's nerves to be stimulated. Yesterday morning, when her husband Chen Pinshan was not in the room, Chen Zhang Juqing got up for no reason and went under the bed, took out a pair of sharp scissors from the dowry box, and stabbed herself in the throat. After stabbing herself, she still lay under the bed. At nearly five o'clock in the morning, Chen Pinshan returned from outside, pushed open the door and entered the room. Not seeing his wife sleeping on the bed, he called out to her but received no response. He did not have time to search and rushed to inform his mother at the Xingfa Inn he had opened. His mother actually said that the new bride had escaped for no reason. She then sent someone to summon the original matchmaker and the bride's father, Zhang Zi'an. First, there was an argument, and then they rushed to the new room to check. Only then did they find the new bride, Zhang Juqing, still lying under the bed, with one foot stretched out. She was wearing red shoes. They called out to her, but there was no response. They dragged her out and saw that her throat was covered in blood, staining her clothes. Without asking the reason, they hired a car and sent her to Renji Hospital for treatment. The hospital reported to the Central Police Station, which informed the French Police Station and sent detectives to the hospital to investigate. They learned that although the woman's throat had two holes poked with scissors, fortunately, the trachea was not severed, and she could still speak, but in a very low voice. The detectives asked the reason for the injury, whether she had been stabbed or had committed suicide. She replied that her mind was vague and unclear. The detectives reported the situation to the police chief. It was heard that Zhang's injury was not serious. The doctor stitched up the wound and kept her in the hospital for treatment. She is expected to be discharged safely in a few days.

Hu Nanshan Pharmacy; Follow-up Inquiry into the Mistaken Prescription; Ding Jinren Has Entered a Comatose State, Upper Body Trembling; Another Doctor, Ni Jinren, Appears in Court to Describe the Incident 136

Ding Jinren, nearly forty years old, a carpenter and the elder brother of Ding Jinrong, a native of Yancheng residing at No. 54, Tan Family Residence, Liyuan Road, Chinese Concession, suddenly suffered from chills and fever on the 20th of last month. He sought treatment from Ling Furen, a doctor from the same village, at No. 191, Rihui East Road, who diagnosed him with damp-heat typhoid fever and prescribed a prescription. Later, Shan Jinrong took the prescription to Hu Nanshan Pharmacy at No. 137, Tei Road, French Concession, to have the medicine prepared. However, Jinren's condition worsened after taking the medicine. Jinrong asked Dr. Ling to come to his home to examine him again and ordered him to take out the original prescription to reconsider and modify it. To his surprise, the prescription that was taken out was not the original prescription that Dr. Ling prescribed, but a prescription for menstruation medicine for a woman surnamed Ding from another doctor, Ni Jinren. He was greatly shocked. After negotiating with the pharmacy without success, Ding Jinrong hired a lawyer and filed a lawsuit with the Second Criminal Court, accusing Hu Zhenxian (over 75 years old, from Yuyao), the owner of Hu Nanshan Pharmacy, his apprentice Sun Longshui (18 years old, from Yuyao), and doctor Ling Furen (27 years old, from Yancheng) of professional negligence resulting in injury and death (Note: the patient Ding Jinren has not yet died), and requested an investigation. After receiving the complaint, the court, on the 11th of this month, had Judge Xiong Huiping open the court and summon all parties for questioning, as detailed in this newspaper. The court had already ordered the police to retrieve the prescriptions for the two patients from the pharmacy. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Xiong opened the court again to continue the hearing. Both parties appeared in court with their lawyers. Patient Ding Jinren was wrapped in a cotton quilt and carried into the courtroom by his brother. Because he could not sit, he lay in the corner of the hearing room behind the audience seats. The court clerk summoned the plaintiff and the defendants to the stand. After briefly questioning their names, the court summoned the witness, another doctor, Ni Jinren. Ni Jinren, residing at No. 158, Dapu Road, stated that on September 11th or 19th, a woman surnamed Ding came to me for medical treatment. The official showed Ni a blue-printed prescription form and asked, "Is this your prescription?" Ni took it and replied, "Yes." The official then took a red-cornered prescription form (the prescription Ling Furen prescribed for Ding Jinren) and asked, "Do you know this prescription?" Ni took it and replied, "I don't know. It's not my prescription." The official asked Ni, "Do you know about this matter?" Ni replied, "I didn't know at first. On the afternoon of September 30th, a detective and someone from the pharmacy came to me to inquire about the woman surnamed Ding who came to see me for treatment and told me to find the group. I only knew that the woman surnamed Ding lived in Yuchang Lane, Caishi Road, but I didn't know the number. I searched but couldn't find her. Later, on October 3rd, I met the family of the woman surnamed Ding on the road and asked them how her condition was after taking the medicine I prescribed. They replied that after taking the medicine, her condition worsened, and she only got better after being treated at the Red Cross Hospital. I then told them about the mistaken prescription and told them to take the prescription to the police station. The police questioned both of us in the police station, said we had nothing to do with the case, and told us to leave. I didn't know what happened after that." Based on Ni's confession, the official ordered him to provide a signed statement and attach it to the file. Patient Ding Jinren was lying in front and could not move. The official then left the stand with the court clerk and went to Ding Jinren's side. The official asked Ding Jinrong to uncover the mattress. Ding Jinren seemed to be asleep. When the quilt was uncovered, he woke up. The official asked his name, age, occupation, and place of origin. He answered with difficulty and stretched out his hand to show his age, but he could not count. The official then asked if he wanted to sue the pharmacy. He shook his head without answering. The official then asked, "Do you not want to sue?" He nodded. The judge, fearing that he did not understand the language, ordered the bailiff to speak to his brother Ding Jin through a translator. Ding Jinren still shook his head in the same way as before, then appeared to be in a comatose state, with his upper body trembling. The official immediately returned to the stand and announced that the case could not be proceeded with for the time being. Defendant Yu Xiufang's lawyer then claimed to the court that he had heard that Ding Jinren only had a mother but no brothers, that they were organized, and requested the court to conduct a detailed investigation. The plaintiff, Ding Jinrong, stated that the defendant had accused him of extortion in the District Court and requested verification. The third defendant, Ling Furen, also stated that they had accused him of organized extortion in the District Court and listed me as the second defendant. Please investigate in detail. The official stated that the case in the District Court was another issue and that you could submit a defense. The second defendant, Longshui, brought two samples of the medicine he had prepared for the patient to present to the court as proof that the medicine was prepared and dispensed according to the prescription. The court ordered that a date be set for another hearing and then adjourned.

South Station Rebuilds Overpass; Estimated Length of 112 Meters, Expected to Be Completed by the End of the Year 138

The various station service projects that have been improved and added to Shanghai South Station of the Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway have been completed one after another. However, the overpass at the station has not yet been rebuilt. Director Huang ordered the Engineering Department to rebuild a steel plate overpass with a length of 112 meters and three escalators connecting the front and rear stations and the platform. The cost of the materials for the project is estimated to be about 5,000 yuan. Construction is scheduled to begin in early November and is expected to be completed by the end of the year. During the construction period, passengers traveling to and from the station will enter and exit through the front door of the station. However, passengers arriving at the station on trains between Longhua and the Shanghai area can still exit through the back door of the station.

Municipal Government Announces Management Rules for Pledged Vehicles in Pawnshops 139

The Municipal Government previously believed that hooligans and thugs in the city often stole vehicles and pledged them in pawnshops, especially bicycles, which were most easily stolen. Therefore, the Social Affairs, Public Security, and Public Utilities Bureaus jointly reviewed and approved eight rules for the management of various vehicles pledged in pawnshops. These rules were approved by the Municipal Government a few days ago and are now being announced for implementation this morning. The original text of the rules is as follows: Rules for the Management of Various Vehicles Pledged in Pawnshops: (1) In addition to complying with the rules stipulated in these rules, each pawnshop should also pay attention to the rules for the management of various vehicles promulgated by the Municipal Government. (2) When pledging various private vehicles, the vehicle registration certificate issued by the Public Utilities Bureau must be handed over to the pawnshop for safekeeping. The pawnshop should also verify whether the steel stamp number specified by the Public Utilities Bureau matches the number on the registration certificate before accepting the pledge. (3) When pledging various commercial vehicles, in addition to complying with the conditions listed in the first clause, the pawnshop must also obtain a written statement from the vehicle company before accepting the pledge. (4) If a pawnshop has any doubts about a pledged vehicle, it should submit the registration certificates to the Public Utilities Bureau for inspection. Pledge is only allowed after the Public Utilities Bureau has verified the certificates. (5) When necessary, the Social Affairs, Public Security, and Public Utilities Bureaus may send personnel to each pawnshop for spot checks at any time. (6) If a pawnshop's procedures are unclear or violate the above rules, it will be punished according to the severity of the circumstances. (7) If there are any matters not covered in these rules, the Social Affairs, Public Security, and Public Utilities Bureaus may jointly amend them temporarily. (8) These rules shall take effect from the date of approval by the Municipal Government.

Public Concession: Meat Market Cold Storage Rental Prices 140

The Public Works Department's Sanitation Office previously constructed a meat market and cold storage facility at the corner of D'Arc Road and Rue Kiao-King Road in Hongkou, next to the Public Works Department Slaughterhouse. The entire project has now been completed and is scheduled to officially open tomorrow (November 1st). The rental fees have been drafted into a memorandum by the head of the Sanitation Office and the veterinarian, reported to the Sanitation Committee, and agreed upon by the head of the Finance Office, submitted to the Public Works Department Board of Directors, and approved for implementation. The general details are as follows: The rental fees for the slaughterhouse cold storage are divided into the following three categories: (A) 3.3 cents of silver per pound every half month. (Ordinary long-term storage or pre-cooling rooms, calculated on a 15-day basis). (B) (6.1 silver dollars per cubic meter per month) Ordinary long-term storage rooms, ranging from 891 to 2,170 cubic feet. (C) Very long-term storage rooms (ice rooms), single cubic meter or double cubic meter, 6 or 12 silver dollars per month. As for the meat market rental fees, the original plan was to open the meat market first without charging rental fees, so that the general butchers could use it themselves. After a considerable period of time, rental fees would be collected. Subsequently, the Deputy Director of the Finance Office, considering that the current prices were already very low, believed that an additional 30% should be added to the existing rates. As a result, the Sanitation Committee decided that the Sanitation and Finance Offices of the Public Works Department should formulate a standard price, charging half the amount from November 1st to the end of the year, and the full amount from January 1st of the following year. The following standard prices have since been set: Cattle and horses, including their appendages, 1.35 silver dollars per head; calves and pigs, including appendages, 70 cents of silver per head; sheep and goats, including appendages, 35 cents of silver per head. The above prices include cold storage convenience and the period shall not exceed seven days. The above prices were approved by the Public Works Department Board of Directors at its regular meeting yesterday.

Public Works Department Band: Special Concert for Young People Held; Inviting Chinese Students to Join the Performance 141

The Public Works Department Music Committee, at its last meeting, discussed the preparation of special concerts suitable for young people and suggested the establishment of singing concerts and preparations for next year's music festival. Regarding the special concert for young people, according to the original proposal of the Public Works Department Band's chief conductor, it was planned to hold four Friday concerts at the Lyceum Theatre within several months of this winter and next spring. However, after the Finance Director reviewed it, he suggested holding two special concerts for young people within this year first, based on the results, to determine whether to proceed next year, as there was a financial loss when this concert was held last year. As a result, the Music Committee accepted the Finance Director's opinion and advocated holding two special concerts for young people this year. The first one will be held on November 8th, and the second one on December 20th. Regarding the establishment of a singing concert, at the previous meeting, a certain gentleman suggested adding singing performances to the Public Works Department Band's performances, and proposed that the Public Works Department hire a Russian singing group. However, it was heard that the required cost was as high as 15,000 to 16,000 silver dollars per year. The Finance Director and the Band's chief conductor both felt that the cost was too high, so the discussion was stopped. Furthermore, regarding next year's music festival, the local Public Works Department Band may be suspended in the spring of next year, so there was a suggestion to issue a general mobilization order to all the musical talents in this city to prepare for the celebration of the festival. The method is to use the Public Works Department Band as the main body, and the local singing groups and other appropriate music groups can be invited to cooperate as appropriate. The Music Committee believes that this proposal is quite insightful and expresses its great approval. However, it feels that it is very difficult to find a suitable rehearsal location. As a result, it was agreed that a preliminary investigation should be started first. It is heard that the above-mentioned measures were all approved at yesterday's regular meeting of the Public Works Department Board of Directors and put on file. Furthermore, the Music Committee expressed its gratitude that the Band's chief conductor recently invited several students from the Chinese National Conservatory of Music to join the Public Works Department Band's performance.

Salary Deduction for Disaster Relief: Sailors Negotiate with China Merchants Bureau, Causing Sailors' Concerns and Determining Donation Methods 142

The army's various districts suffered from floods, and all civil servants must have half a month's salary deducted and deducted in two installments. The sailors serving on various merchant ships in this city, especially the drivers and machinists on the Jianghai ships of the state-owned China Merchants Bureau, received an order from the Ministry. Because the sailors are technical personnel, they are not within the scope of civil servants as a rule, and it does not seem appropriate to deduct their salaries for disaster relief. However, for the sake of disaster relief, everyone has sympathy, and the sailors will donate voluntarily. However, the Bureau instructed that all sailors must still have half a month's salary deducted for disaster relief and deducted from October. When the sailors received the news, they went to the Machinist and Driver Guilds, requesting that a letter be sent to the China Merchants Bureau, which firmly believed that sailors were forced to be civil servants and ordered to deduct their salaries for disaster relief. However, the sailors work on the sea, away from their hometowns. They do not have the pleasure of a home all year round and fight in the wind and waves all year round, and their monthly salaries are very low. Their monthly income and expenses are already fixed. Now that half a month's salary is deducted, the sailors will be affected economically. They have asked the guild to send a letter to the Bureau, requesting that the sailors' double salaries that should have been received over the years be deducted from the deposit as disaster relief donations. They are willing to help for half a month at a time and not deduct it from their current monthly salaries so as not to affect their livelihoods. However, the two guilds sent several letters, but the Bureau did not reply or express whether it agreed or disagreed. The sailors were very angry and went to the two guilds again yesterday, asking them to send another letter to the Bureau for a final question. If the Bureau still does not reply, it is considered to be deliberately making things difficult. The sailors will not recognize the deducted salary, no matter what, and order it to reply soon to avoid disputes.

Second Special Court Destroys Narcotics by Burning 147

The Second Special District Local Court of Jiangsu and Shanghai, according to the precedent, publicly burns confiscated opium, smoking paraphernalia, and narcotics such as morphine, heroin, and red pills, as well as gambling paraphernalia seized by the French police every three months. Before June of this year, fifteen burnings had already been carried out. Now, the various items confiscated from the July-September narcotics and gambling cases will be burned by court president Gan Simao and chief prosecutor Qiao Wanxuan, who have jointly scheduled the sixteenth burning on the 30th of this month (yesterday). The court reported to the Third High Branch Court and the Ministry of Justice Administration in advance, and sent letters to various institutions and legal groups in Shanghai, inviting representatives to supervise the event. Yesterday was the appointed date. The Second Special Court arranged the site the day before. The location was still on the open space next to the court's east side. Yesterday morning, all kinds of items were moved to the site and arranged. At 2:00 PM, the president of the Second High Branch Court of Jiangsu, Jia Yi, and representatives from various institutions and groups arrived successively. President Wang, Chief Qiao, and Secretary Li greeted them and offered tea and refreshments. Yang Ding, a servant, was ordered to move the narcotics in front of the representatives. After inspection, they were piled up in the site, stacked with pine wood, poured with kerosene, and sprinkled with salt. The fire was lit to burn. After the narcotics were burned, gambling paraphernalia and contraband were burned. The items burned in this session were gradually reduced compared to previous sessions. The event was completed at 4:00 PM. The representatives left and took their leave. This session burned sixty-five sets of smoking paraphernalia, five pounds and eight ounces of opium, and forty-two small packets, thirty-two small boxes of opium paste, and half a jar, sixty-two thousand one hundred and seventeen red pills, one hundred and fifty-six opium bubbles, one pound of morphine, and two ounces and five qian, and ten small packets, nineteen small packets of heroin, eighty-seven pounds of white powder, and one box, one hundred and one red pill cloth bags, nine hundred and thirty paper bags, thirty-six smoking pipes, and other instruments for manufacturing red pills and morphine. There were also thirty-three Huahui cards, ten sets of playing cards, twenty-five cards, five sets of mahjong tiles, fifty-two dominoes, thirteen dice, and three counterfeit toy guns, one counterfeit wooden toy gun, thirty measuring poles, a small stack of counterfeit trademark paper, and other items not detailed, totaling two hundred and seventy-one pieces. The ashes were left overnight and will be transported to the ocean in burlap bags today. The copper, lead, aluminum, and other materials that could not be burned were all destroyed.

Yang Xixiang Sentenced for Instigating Arson 149

Yang Xiji Foreign Goods Store and Baosen Shen Zhuang, located at No. 6 Lane 9, Taiwan Road, were established by Yang Bixiang and Xu Minghua from Ningbo, respectively. Baosen was insured for 1,000 yuan of fire insurance with the North American Insurance Company, while Yang Xiji was insured for 7,000 yuan with the Haohua and Xiangtai Insurance Company. At 4:30 AM on the 19th of this month, a fire suddenly broke out in the two shops. The Fire Department made every effort to extinguish the fire, preventing it from spreading to the neighbors. However, after an investigation by Chinese detectives Pang Ruiqing, Bao Sun Dafa, and Chen Ruisheng of the Laozha Gate Police Station, it was discovered that there were suspicions of arson. Yang and Xu were arrested, along with Yang Xiji's accountant Tong Binhou and apprentices Hu Xiangsheng and Xu Mingcai from Baosen, and sent to the First Special District Court for interrogation and custody. The details have been recorded in this newspaper. After an investigation by the police station, it was learned that the arson was instigated by Yang Xixiang in order to claim the insurance money. He secretly arranged for Zhu Wusheng, who was on the run, to start the fire. He had previously notified Tong Binhou and instructed him not to destroy the evidence. However, Xu Minghua, Xu Mingcai, and Hu Xiangsheng did not participate in the premeditation. Only Yang Xixiang and Tong Binhou were prosecuted according to Article 173 of the Criminal Law. Xu and the other three were not prosecuted. The interrogation by the First Special Court has been concluded. Yesterday morning, Judge Qian Hongye took the bench and sentenced Yang Xixiang to three years and six months in prison for instigating arson and destroying an inhabited building. Tong Binhou was sentenced to ten months in prison for assisting in arson and destroying an inhabited building, suspended for three years. After checking the kerosene-soaked cloth, Police Lawyer Wang Yaotang requested that Tong still be required to pay a 300-yuan guarantee during the appeal period. The judge approved.

Wang Meizhen, originally named Wang Meizhen, a 19-year-old Qingyi actress performing in the Dajing Troupe at the Great World Amusement Park, and Wu Junshan, a 30-year-old Jiaxing native who sang Wusheng in the Great World Beijing Opera Theater, were cousins and fellow apprentices. Ye Jingchun Dies from Vomiting Blood 151

Ye Jingchun, 45 years old, a native of Ningbo, was an employee of the International Radio Station of the Ministry of Transportation in this city. At around 6:00 PM last night, Ye went alone to the hot spring bathhouse on Edward Road. About half an hour later, he came out happily. Unexpectedly, after walking a few steps, Ye suddenly felt nauseous, as if he wanted to vomit. He leaned against the wall and vomited. Unexpectedly, he vomited fresh blood, which could not be stopped. He immediately fell to the ground unconscious. Fortunately, the police on duty caught a glimpse of him and quickly took him to the hospital for treatment. However, he died on the way. The police were notified to send the body to the coroner's office for examination and to investigate the deceased's family.

Robbery at Fan Deyu's Home on Wusong Road 153

Fan Deyu, a Ningbo native who sells beef at No. 110 Wusong Road, Hongkou, was robbed at around 6:30 AM yesterday. When his daughter was washing the urinal at the back door, four robbers wearing blue cloth shirts and pants, speaking with a local accent, suddenly went to rob. Only one of the robbers had a handgun. He first placed the woman under surveillance and then rushed upstairs, threatening the victim to hand over the box keys and searching separately. After about half an hour, they all escaped with their loot. As a result, more than 400 yuan was robbed. Afterwards, the victim reported to the Qiukou Police Station in charge, requesting a pursuit.

Buying a Coffin with a Bad Check: He Benyao's Actions Border on Fraud 154

In August, He Benyao, a native of Zhenjiang who resided at No. 384 Fangbang Road and worked as a runner, introduced his fellow villager He Ronggen to Li Junfu, the owner of the Xinhua Xiang Shouxuqi Shop at Erpailou in the city, to purchase a coffin, agreeing on a price of 64 yuan. At that time, only 40 yuan in cash was paid, and a bank check was issued for August 10th. When it was due, it was found to be worthless and was a bad check. When the introducer was pursued to return the money, he was nowhere to be found. Later, He Benyao was found and persuaded to issue a guarantee for the payment. However, it was still equal to zero. At 11:00 AM yesterday, He Benyao found He Ronggen and sent him to Xinhua Xiang. The shop owner sent a representative, Wang Rongtang, to hand him over to the Yimiao Police Station for investigation. After questioning, Chief Liu learned that He Ronggen had purchased the coffin with a bad check, which was intentional fraud. He was ordered to be sent to the General Bureau for interrogation.

Missing Female Worker Wang Abao: Tang Fuxiang Denies Any Relationship 155

Wang Yan, a 39-year-old woman from Haining who lived in the Jiangjiabang area of Gaolang Bridge, was working at the Lanyin Weitong Yarn Factory. On May 18th of this year, she suddenly went missing. On the 23rd of this month, Chinese detectives Jin Wanrong and Liu Zhisheng of the Yulin Road Police Station found her in the workshop at No. 31 Hengfeng Yarn Factory on Huasheng Road. They took her to the police station along with her lover, Tang Fuxiang, a native of Shanghai. The woman was taken back by her mother, and Tang was sent to the First Special District Court for interrogation. He denied any relationship with the woman, while Abao insisted that she was 21 years old and born in the Year of the Tiger. Her mother said she was 19 years old. Tang Fuxiang was ordered to be remanded in custody for further verification with witnesses. Yesterday morning, Judge Jiang Shuzi arrived at Criminal Division No. 3 to continue the trial. The Public Works Department lawyer, Zhang Shuaizhu, stated that he had obtained information from the landlord of the workshop that the house was rented by the woman. However, the defendant often stayed there or stayed overnight. He presented the letters and postcards exchanged between him and the woman. The landlord, surnamed Yu, claimed that the house was rented by Abao in June. Later, her brother stayed with his sister for about two months, and the defendant often came too. Abao said that her mother also came to stay for about a month in August. She claimed that she had no sexual relationship with the defendant. When questioned, the defendant claimed that the letters were replies to his sister's business inquiries and firmly denied having a physical relationship with Abao. Attorney Yan Ze defended him. Judge Mei Shuzi ordered him to remain in custody pending sentencing.

First Draft of "Comprehensive Treatise on the Spring and Autumn Annals" Published 160

The "Spring and Autumn Annals" occupies an important position in Chinese scholarship. Scholars throughout history have argued endlessly, but those who have traced its origins and established their own unique banner are very few. It is now heard that the Zhen Society in Hangzhou has published a book entitled "Comprehensive Treatise on the Spring and Autumn Annals," which is the first draft written by Mao Qi of Dinghai. The entire book is divided into four chapters: (1) Confucius and the Spring and Autumn Annals; (2) The Beginning and End of the Spring and Autumn Annals; (3) The Authors of the Commentaries; (4) The Teachings of the Spring and Autumn Annals. Each chapter is based on extensive evidence and presents new theories with insightful observations. For example, it argues that the "Spring and Autumn Annals" is the "Lu Spring and Autumn Annals," that Confucius only wrote commentaries on the Spring and Autumn Annals, that Guliang was written for Shen Gong, and that Quyang was written for Humu Sheng. It also argues that the teachings of the Spring and Autumn Annals lie in governing the world, and that it elucidates the complete personality of Confucius, all of which are unprecedented insights. It also makes many corrections to the theories of recent scholars such as Zhang Taiyan. In today's rectification of national studies, where specialized works on the Spring and Autumn Annals are rarely heard, this book deserves attention. The price is seventy cents, and it is sold by Shanghai and various local Shenghuo bookstores.

Lawyer Liu Yixiang, a graduate of Tokyo Imperial University, specialized in ophthalmology and established a clinic at 6 Malishi New Village. Literary figures such as Shen Yinmo of Peking University, Guan Jianan of Minbao, and Mi Gegu of Chenbao were all cured by him. Recently, Mr. Jiachen of Jingbao was on the verge of blindness, but after Liu injected his own blood serum into his sclera, he was completely cured. Countless other figures from political, academic, industrial, and commercial circles have been cured by him. He is truly a master.

Educational News

The First Sign of Closer Sino-Japanese Cultural Education: Japan's Boxer Indemnity, 1.72 Million Yuan Annually, Subsidizes Exchange Students Between China and Japan 164

(Special dispatch from Beiping) Amidst the calls for Sino-Japanese economic cooperation, Japan plans to carry out Sino-Japanese educational and cultural undertakings. According to sources, the Japanese Boxer Indemnity, amounting to 1.72 million Japanese yen annually, has been entirely managed and distributed by the Bureau of Chinese Cultural Affairs of the Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs since 1931. Because the Japanese found it inconvenient to proceed alone, they organized the Sino-Japanese Cultural Committee. It was expected that the committee's authority would be determined during the second Sino-Japanese General Committee meeting in Beiping, making it an independent cultural organization. However, the Japanese side refused to discuss it, citing the Japanese National Assembly Act and the Japanese Accounting Law. As a result, the hope of using the Japanese Boxer Indemnity to subsidize Sino-Japanese cultural undertakings was suspended for ten years. Currently, some Chinese and Japanese educators advocate dividing the Japanese Boxer Indemnity into two parts. One part would subsidize Chinese students studying in Japan, and a committee jointly organized by various provinces in North China would select university graduates to study science and engineering in Japan. The other part of the Japanese Boxer Indemnity would subsidize Japanese students' expenses for books and tours while studying geology, literature, and history at Chinese universities. It is heard that this is currently being pursued in Beiping.

Ministry of Education Explains Compilation of Educational Laws and Regulations 165

The Ministry of Education has compiled and published several matters regarding educational laws and regulations that were previously submitted by various provinces and cities for explanation and have been separately instructed but not yet published in newspapers. One item is that the Jiangxi Education Department inquired about "The Provisional Regulations for Teacher Certification in Secondary Schools and Normal Schools, regarding the qualifications of various types of teachers, all have regulations on several years of teaching experience after graduating from a certain school. If the school where they have taught is a primary school, can they apply for certification as a junior high school teacher? If it is a junior high school, can they apply for certification as a senior high school teacher? Should the subject they have taught be limited to the subject they studied at university or institute?" The response was: (1) Regarding the so-called teaching experience in the Provisional Regulations for Teacher Certification in Secondary Schools and Normal Schools, for graduates from specialized or higher institutions, the teaching experience is not limited to what level of school. For graduates from schools equivalent to senior vocational or middle school level, the teaching experience should be limited to secondary schools. (2) The subject they have taught is not limited to the subject they studied at university or specialized school. Another item is that the Shandong Education Department inquired "What are the examination subjects for those who take the labor and household affairs subjects in the Middle School Teacher Certification Examination?" The response was: The specialized examination subjects for household affairs in the Middle School Teacher Certification Examination are (1) Family Economics and Management, (2) Family Hygiene, (3) Child Rearing Methods. The specialized examination subjects for labor (crafts) are (1) Introduction to Materials and Tools, (2) Drawing Work Diagrams, (3) Practical Production. The specialized examination subjects for labor (agriculture) are (1) Crop Science, (2) Horticulture, (3) Afforestation, (4) Animal Husbandry. Another item is that the Shanghai Education Bureau, based on a request from the private Shanghai Kindergarten Normal School to confirm the qualifications of its graduates, was instructed that the qualifications of graduates from the undergraduate program of the school are equivalent to those of graduates from normal schools, and the qualifications of graduates from the short-term program of the school are equivalent to those of graduates from simplified normal schools. Another item is the explanation of the Secondary Education Statistical Table and various school survey forms issued by the Ministry in the 13th year of the Republic: (1) The words "county and city" before the word "established" in the title of the survey form should be deleted. All national, provincial, municipal, county, and private secondary schools should fill them out separately according to their respective establishment. (2) The number of classes in the class and student column on the survey form refers to the number of classes in each grade. (3) The blank space under the total of the junior and senior high school graduates column on the survey form is for schools to fill in the classes of a certain subject or other types of schools attached. If the schools do not have separate subjects or attached other types of classes, they should fill them in under the total. (4) The three words "more school numbers" in Article 2 of the instructions for filling out the survey form should be deleted. (5) According to the regulations for vocational schools promulgated by the Ministry, the midwifery department is classified under the household affairs category, and midwifery schools should be included in household affairs vocational schools.

Li Jinxi of the National Language Council Elaborates on the Ministry of Education's Efforts to Promote Phonetic Chinese Characters, the Selection of Characters Took Four Months to Complete, the Implementation Method of Nine Articles Promulgated by the Ministry of Education

Mr. Li Jinxi, a standing committee member of the National Language Promotion Council, recently published a detailed account of the Ministry of Education's efforts to promote phonetic Chinese characters. A reporter from the Shanghai News Agency has specially recorded it as follows:

The Purpose of Casting and its Process, In November of the 23rd year of the Republic, the 39th regular meeting of the Preparatory Committee for National Language Unification of the Ministry of Education passed the proposal made by Committee Member Li Jinxi that a bronze mold for phonetic annotation of Chinese characters should be cast by the state. The proposal was submitted to the Ministry for review. In January of the 24th year, the Ministry adopted this proposal, convened a discussion meeting, and subsequently decided to allocate funds to entrust a business to cast the mold. On March 5th, the 202nd Executive Yuan meeting passed the proposal submitted by the Ministry to sign a contract with the Zhonghua Book Company to create a square-shaped typeface by attaching phonetic symbols to the side of the company's existing imitation Song long-style characters. In order to facilitate the printing of reading materials needed for short-term compulsory education and mass education, the Ministry first cast a No. 2 typeface, and then No. 3, No. 5, and No. 4 typefaces, completing the entire set of bronze molds within approximately one year. However, the molds cast by the Ministry were only to show promotion and to promote the phonetic Chinese characters. Businesses were also free to cast their own, but the style of the phonetic symbol mother mold must be shown to be standard to avoid misrepresentation. Therefore, the former National Language Council passed the proposal made by Committee Member Li Jinxi at the 43rd regular meeting on March 3rd, requesting the Ministry of Education to issue two types of typeface printing style methods for phonetic symbols for annotating Chinese characters and for independent use. After being passed, it was submitted to the Ministry and reviewed and printed into a booklet called "Phonetic Symbol Printing Style," which was promulgated in April for compliance.

The Selection of Phonetic Chinese Characters, In March of the 24th year, the Ministry entrusted a business to cast the bronze mold for phonetic Chinese characters, and instructed the former National Language Council to quickly select the Chinese characters for this project. Regarding the number of Chinese characters for this project, there were approximately three opinions: (1) It was advocated that the phonetic Chinese characters should be used as a method of limiting the number of characters used, and a basic set of Chinese characters should be established, with approximately 1,100 characters. (2) It was advocated that the number of characters needed in objective reality should be the scope, with approximately 3,000 characters commonly used by children and the masses. First, cast the combined commonly used characters, and at most 6,000 to 7,000 characters, and then increase the casting. (3) It was advocated that all Chinese characters should be annotated with phonetics, and the more uncommon the characters, the more appropriate it is to determine the pronunciation and annotate them. In the future, all old books should be printed with phonetic Chinese characters, so that everyone can recite and read them. The National Language Council established a special group meeting and decided to adopt the second opinion as the selection principle. Based on this principle, the most economical method was used to select the characters. First, various vocabularies that met this principle were written on separate cards, character by character, and arranged and organized in the order of the commonly used Chinese character vocabulary in the National Language. This selection work lasted from March to the end of June and included 6,788 characters, which is the total number of characters in the phonetic Chinese character typeface.

Textbooks specializing in teaching phonetic symbols are prepared for primary school remedial classes and short-term literacy classes, as well as preliminary learning for mass education. However, it is also not permissible to mechanically learn the alphabet, but to spell simple and meaningful words and sentences. Because phonetic Chinese characters can promote children's and the masses' ability to read, recite, and practice writing, their effect is greater than simplified characters, which only facilitate writing. Therefore, attention should be paid to making appropriate preparations. On September 3rd, the Ministry of Education formulated nine implementation methods to facilitate promotion. This is the entire process.

Nine Implementation Methods Prescribed by the Ministry of Education, Attached are the nine articles of the Ministry of Education's promulgated Promotion of Phonetic Chinese Characters: (1) All texts in textbooks for mass schools and short-term primary schools must be entirely in phonetic Chinese characters. (2) The new word list in the Chinese language textbook for elementary primary schools must be entirely in phonetic Chinese characters. (3) The textbooks for social studies, nature (or general knowledge) in elementary primary schools, and the textbooks for Chinese language, social studies (geography and history), nature, and hygiene in advanced primary schools should be entirely in phonetic Chinese characters. (4) Starting from the first semester of the first grade of elementary primary school, phonetic symbols should be taught first, and after practice becomes proficient, then the Chinese text should be taught. In the future, all newly compiled Chinese language textbooks for elementary primary schools should compile a separate first volume before the first volume, dedicated to phonetic symbols, compiled into stories, for teaching purposes. The teaching method should be based on first synthesis and then analysis. The above regulations may be temporarily modified and implemented by local educational administrative agencies in areas where there is a shortage of teachers to teach phonetic symbols. (5) Starting from July of the 25th year of the Republic, all newly compiled textbooks and books for elementary schools and mass schools must comply with these regulations, otherwise they will not be approved.

Phonetic Chinese Character Promotion Method, In January of the 24th year, the Ministry decided to allocate funds to cast the bronze mold for phonetic Chinese characters. In March, the 43rd regular meeting of the former National Language Council passed the proposal made by Committee Member Li Jinxi and others, requesting the Ministry of Education to stipulate that all textbooks for various subjects in primary schools and reading materials for children and the masses should be printed with phonetic Chinese characters. After being passed, it was submitted to the Ministry for review and implementation. In June, when the Ministry convened a meeting to discuss the first batch of simplified character lists, the original proposer of this case collected opinions from all parties on this case, and finally summarized them into eight points and reported them to the Ministry for reference. (1) In the main text of the official primary school Chinese language textbooks, new characters should be printed with this typeface, and non-new characters should not. The reason is that each subject in primary school teaching has its own main purpose. One of the purposes of the Chinese language subject is to practice writing. Chinese character teaching requires mandatory memorization. If non-new characters are also annotated with phonetics, children will lose the opportunity for mandatory memorization, which is not in line with the purpose of this subject. (2) The textbooks for all subjects other than Chinese language in the lower-level primary schools, i.e., arithmetic, social studies, nature, and hygiene, should all be printed with this typeface. Because the teaching of these subjects each has its own main purpose, the purpose is not to practice language. Therefore, all characters should be annotated with phonetics to avoid reducing the efficiency of teaching this subject due to language barriers. (3) All extracurricular reading materials used in official primary schools and short-term literacy classes, as well as all reading materials and textbooks used in mass education, must be absolutely printed with this typeface to facilitate reading and increase knowledge. (4) Briefly discuss with the Shanghai publishing industry that in the future, Chinese language textbooks for elementary primary schools should compile a separate first volume, which uses only phonetic symbols to spell simple words and sentences, so that children can fully recognize phonetic symbols before reading the text of Chinese characters. Also, compile separately (6) All levels of normal schools in various provinces and cities should teach phonetic symbols, so that normal school graduates have the skills to teach phonetic symbols. (7) During the transition period, all primary schools must set aside a portion of the time in the Chinese language subject to specialize in teaching phonetic symbols. (8) Starting from January of the 25th year of the Republic, all editors of reading materials for children and the masses must print them with phonetic Chinese characters. (9) The Ministry and the educational administrative agencies of various provinces and cities should encourage all newspapers to print with phonetic Chinese characters as much as possible within the possible scope.

Scout Association Anniversary Week, City Scouts Hold Celebration Ceremony, Tomorrow at 1:00 PM at the Nanshi Stadium 167

The Chinese Boy Scout movement has been around for 24 years since its inception in the first year of the Republic. During this period, it has experienced times of prosperity and decline. Since the 17th year of the Republic, it has been effectively led and managed by our Party, and after the establishment of the Boy Scout Headquarters, the national Boy Scout movement has advanced according to regulations. The Chinese Boy Scouts, which used to be scattered, disorganized, and independent, gradually moved towards unification of organization and training. At that time, the Party Boy Scout Commander took the position that the headquarters organization only shouldered the responsibility of leading the Boy Scouts towards unification. He vigorously advocated the general association system. He first obtained the support of Mr. Dai Jitao, and on April 14th of the 21st year of the Republic, he submitted the organizational plan to the Central Standing Committee, which was approved. A general association preparatory office was first established, and on November 1st of the 23rd year of the Republic, the official establishment of the Chinese Boy Scout General Association was announced. However, time flies, and one year has passed since the establishment of the General Association. Under the leadership of the General Association, all Boy Scouts in the country are happy and inspired, showing a new atmosphere. The City Scout Council has received the order from the General Association and has decided to hold a celebration ceremony tomorrow (November 1st) at 1:00 PM at the City Sports Stadium on Dajilu, Nanshi. Each troop will send two or more members in uniform to participate in the celebration. There will be a grand occasion at that time.

縣眾安鄉　昨開二次普教會議　各校明日一律開學 172

The Second General Education Conference in Zhong'an Township, Shanghai County, Was Held Yesterday; All Schools Will Begin Classes Uniformly Tomorrow.

Shanghai County's compulsory literacy education is scheduled to begin on November 1st. The popular literacy education committees of various townships and towns have also been established one after another. The Zhong'an Township Popular Literacy Education Committee held its second meeting yesterday. The attendees were Lu Shu'ang, Zhou Wenyao, Cai Zaoshi, Weng Gongyu, Shi Yong (Jin Lin representing Lin Rong), Zhang Fengshan, Zheng Shaoyuan, Lu Liran, Wu Yao, Ni Binzhi, Zhu Zongming, He Guixiang, Ru Bocai, Liu Caiyu, Du Zhanyun and fifteen other people. Zhang Fengshan and Ru Bocai were recommended as heads of the general affairs section. Chairman Zhou Wenyao and Zheng Shaoyuan were recommended as directors of the design and instruction section. Lu Shu'ang and Zhu Zongming were recommended as directors of the investigation and assessment section. 3. The first and second wards will be organized by Zhong'an Elementary School to host one class each. The third ward will be organized by the People's Education Center to host one class. The fourth, fifth, and sixth wards will be organized by Xianqiao Elementary School to host three classes. The seventh ward, Shanhongying Second Elementary School will host two classes. 4. The Zhong'an Township Office will be responsible for distributing the school supplies for each school. 5. The design and instruction section will be responsible for drafting the daily class schedule. 6. Each school is scheduled to begin classes on November 1st. 7. The next meeting will still be convened by Zhang Shangxi at a scheduled time.

Team Leader's Remarks: Yesterday, according to Lu Qihua, the head delegate of the team, told a reporter from the Guoguang News Agency that because Guangxi Province is located in a remote western region with inconvenient transportation, sports were still in their infancy. Recently, under the vigorous promotion of sports by Provincial Chairman Huang Xuchu, sports have gradually developed and are becoming more militarized. Guangxi had not participated in the previous five National Games, so this year's was a groundbreaking first. The only events participated in were long-distance running and swimming. Due to the economic and terrain conditions in Guangxi Province, it is not easy to develop ball sports. Swimming, mountain climbing, and long-distance running are more common. This time returning south, more attention should be paid to sports, and they should be actively promoted in order to make progress. In addition, our team came to Shanghai to participate in the National Games, and our skills are still immature. We sincerely hope that our compatriots will give us guidance. Staying here for a month, we have received warm greetings from all walks of life. It is especially reluctant to say goodbye today.

小男兒（八）（〇） 188

Little Men (8) (〇)

— Original by Ms. Alcott of the United States, Translated by Zheng Xiaocang

Who knew that she would reply fiercely, "Who wants to come! Not me; what gentlemen! I hate these boys!" Her hand was still hurting a lot, so she began to regret that she shouldn't have been so reckless just now, and realized that she could have used a smarter method to express her anger.

"Alas, you hate my boys? That's unfortunate. In fact, when they are willing, they are not unable to take care of politeness and make others feel comfortable. True politeness exists in the attitude, and thoughtfulness of others in words and deeds. This is something everyone can have, as long as they are willing to treat others the way they hope others will treat them."

Mrs. Pei seemed to be talking to Nan'en, but the children explained it to each other with their elbows, and it seemed that they could understand the point quite well, at least at that time, because they passed the butter dishes to their neighbors, saying "Please," and "Thank you," "Yes, sir," "No, miss," etc., really polite. Nan'en didn't say a word, just kept quiet, wanting to tickle her neighbor but never dared to, because he was so solemn. She seemed to have forgotten her hatred for the boys at this time, and played the "I see you" game with them until dark. During the game, someone would often give her their candy stick to taste, which clearly made her temper better, because the last words she said before going to sleep were:

"After my son and I get the boards, I will let you play."
