Shen Bao Guohuo Weekly

發展國貨前途的幾項重要工作 189

Several Important Tasks for the Development of the Future of Domestic Products

— Xuan Wan

As everyone knows, at present, if we want to save the Chinese national economy from danger and death, and put many people struggling on the line of bankruptcy and death into a state of living and working in peace and contentment, we can only take the road of developing domestic products and revitalizing industry. This is the only correct direction. However, in recent years, the progress of domestic products cannot be said to be weak, but the future of domestic products is undoubtedly still struggling on a very difficult road. Objective environmental obstructions and obstacles are heavy. What is the reason for this? Here, I hope everyone will never attribute it to the saying of fate, but know that the success of domestic products is by no means a matter of overnight. It really requires us to have greater courage to work hard and struggle, and to open up a new path from the dark road.

We can see several problems facing the domestic product industry at the present stage, such as narrow sales, overproduction, stagnation of economic turnover rate, and the obstruction of outward expansion of the market. These are all great regrets. On the other hand, we can see those foreign factories set up in China. In addition to their strong capital and large equipment, they also pay attention to the quality of their products, the sales methods, and the convenience of transportation methods, which make us feel beyond our reach. Therefore, I deeply feel that in the current progress of the future of domestic products, in addition to working hard to develop outward, it seems that there is still a need to pay attention to industrial organization, management methods, and production technology. Now I will write down the above points, hoping that the entire industrial community will quickly pay attention and implement them:

First, improve production technology. In recent years, domestic products have become more and more exquisite due to the encouragement of people from all walks of life. However, due to the competition of the same industry, it is inevitable that they have to make up for it by cutting corners and reducing materials. From now on, we should resolutely get rid of this behavior of quenching thirst with poison, and should strive to improve production technology. On the one hand, we should reduce costs and lower prices, and on the other hand, we should adapt to the needs of customers and strive to make the products exquisite.

Second, strive for financial cooperation. The trend of economic depression has made the financial community tighten loans to industries. In this crisis, the domestic product community should thoroughly cooperate with the financial community to open up a way out. At present, the following should be implemented first: (1) Replace the current credit loans with the discounting of commercial acceptance drafts, (2) Replace the current movable property pledge loans with bank acceptance drafts, (3) Replace the current factory base pledge loans with the acceptance of company debt notes.

Third, promote domestic raw materials. Manufacturers engaged in domestic product industries should try their best to use domestic raw materials. At the same time, they should find ways to develop and promote raw materials that are not yet available in China, so that they can not only prevent huge leaks but also increase rural income, which is to promote the purchasing power of domestic products among general farmers.

Fourth, study transportation convenience. In the future, the way out for domestic products will undoubtedly be in the border provinces and overseas markets. The study of transportation methods is very important. We should study and implement how to make freight rates low, and how to prevent goods from being damaged in transit, and how to ensure speed.

Originally, there are many ways to develop domestic products, and establishing the reputation of domestic products is especially the primary plan. We must gain the unanimous confidence of the people of the whole country in domestic products and create the strongest foundation for the future of the national industry.

Reducing Costs is the Key to National Goods' Survival 190

— Yang An

Recently, Mr. Yuan Bingyuan returned from a factory inspection trip to Europe and America. When a reporter asked him about his impressions of inspecting industries in fifteen countries, Mr. Gu said that all countries are making tireless efforts to produce and expand overseas markets. Countries such as Germany, England, Sweden, Austria-Hungary, the United States, and Japan are particularly focused on refining their manufacturing, aiming solely to reduce costs and offer lower prices. There are many methods to achieve lower prices, but a consistent focus on training technical talent and striving for scientific management is a common trend. Particularly commendable is the industry of Czechoslovakia. The operation of the Bata shoe factory resembles an industrial complex, with the entire factory forming a self-contained district. It employs no fewer than 30,000 workers. Workers' housing, consumer goods, public utilities, and public entertainment are all managed by the company through bulk purchases and retail distribution. As a result, the living standards of workers are lower compared to areas outside the industrial zone. The same worker, working at the Bata factory, earns a monthly wage of 50 yuan, while outside, it would require 70 or 80 yuan. Therefore, workers are willing to work at the factory, which implicitly reduces many costs. This is why Bata shoes are invincible worldwide. As for scientific management, while it emphasizes the precision of machinery and the training of personnel, and the seriousness of time economy, the meticulousness, lack of perfunctoriness, and lack of procrastination in handling matters are also worthy of emulation by our national goods industry. In various countries' business sectors, from the government to the managers and staff of factories and shops, there is a consistent emphasis on precise calculations, adherence to time, and the utmost seriousness and speed in handling matters, which is truly admirable. In Italy and Germany, since Mussolini and Hitler came to power, the intensity of work is visible everywhere. Even regarding the issue of not delaying documents, there is an interesting anecdote to tell: they advocate not using drawers in office desks, believing that having drawers often leads to placing pending matters inside, thinking that if it is not done today, it can wait until tomorrow. As more and more accumulates, it becomes difficult to handle and is seen as a problem, and there is never hope for swift progress in any endeavor. Therefore, everyone believes that drawers are obstacles in handling matters, and it is better to abolish them directly. Although this is a small detail, it has great value for adoption or research in scientific management. I am also introducing it to inform my comrades in the national goods industry.

The National Goods Movement in the Past Month 191

— Ba Ling

In the national goods movement of the past month, I feel that there are several things that need to be brought up and discussed. I will write them down one by one below and add my personal opinions, hoping that our national goods future is not without hope, as long as people are willing to work hard and those in power are willing to genuinely promote it.

(1) The Social Bureau Strictly Regulates the Organization of National Goods Markets: The rise of national goods markets in the past year can be said to have been a great trend for a time. From the perspective of promoting national goods, it seems to be a good phenomenon. However, according to newspaper reports, disputes have occurred in national goods markets in many places, such as Nantong and Wuxi, due to unsound organizations. This is a regrettable matter and greatly hinders the future promotion of national goods. Now, the Social Bureau, in view of this, has specifically and strictly stipulated the organizational regulations for national goods markets, with thoughtful considerations, which can prevent the occurrence of disputes in national goods markets in the future and increase the general public's good impression of national goods and markets. This is also a gratifying thing.

(2) The Guangdong Education Department Bans Student Decorations: The Guangdong Education Department has three regulations for the decorations of students in the province, instructing them to be uniformly observed: (1) Students must wear clothes made of national goods materials; (2) Female students must not perm their hair; (3) The use of cosmetics and wearing high heels are prohibited, etc. As the Student National Goods Year is about to end, the Guangdong Education Department's attention to this is something we cannot regard as a mere formality. We hope that other provincial education authorities will also proceed in unison to achieve a final grand effect for the Student National Goods Year.

(3) Liang Tongfang and Others Organize a National Goods Promotion Group: Patriotic individuals such as Liang Tongfang, in order to promote the sale of national goods, specially united with many like-minded people to organize a National Goods Promotion Group. On the one hand, they solicited national goods from various factories and national goods organizations, and on the other hand, they hired national goods industry leaders such as Lin Kanghou, Wang Xiaolai, Pan Yangyao, and Fang Yexian as consultants to provide guidance as needed. This is very worthy of emulation and promotion by young people who love to use national goods.

(4) The General Labor Union Organizes a National Goods Sales Team: The Shanghai General Labor Union, in order to relieve unemployed workers, specially contacted various factories to organize a national goods sales team, both to relieve workers' unemployment and to promote the sales of national goods by French law. It is a good thing to kill two birds with one stone.

(5) The Social Bureau Bans Foreign Names for National Goods: The use of foreign languages for national goods is indeed a very shameful thing. The Social Bureau is currently dispatching personnel to secretly investigate and will ban the use of foreign names for national goods. This has a great relationship with the psychological construction aspect of promoting national goods.

As mentioned above, I feel that in the national goods movement of the past month, there has been obvious progress. Therefore, I do not hesitate to express it, and I inform those who generally care about the national goods movement.

National Goods Wool Yarn 192

— Rong Yu

The weather is gradually getting colder, and the sales of wool yarn are about to surge again. Don't think this is a small thing, people's needs for it are even greater than for cotton and leather goods. Because it suits everyone's taste, both the poor and the rich like it; and the things made from it, both men and women, old and young, can use, such as shirts, pants, hats, socks, gloves, scarves, and women's coats, etc. Think about how much of it is needed in a year!

The reason why wool yarn is popular is first and foremost because it is strong and durable, so economical housewives all like it. Think about making a set of cotton-padded clothes for a child. Although the price is cheap, the child will jump around and damage it in at most one or two years; a set of wool yarn clothes, no matter how you wear it, will last at least five years. So, isn't wool yarn cheaper than cotton cloth! Moreover, wool yarn is elastic, so it doesn't matter if it's made a little smaller; it doesn't matter if it's made a little bigger. It's not like cotton cloth, which can't be worn if it's too small; and it's not warm enough if it's too big. Because of this, it has increased people's welcome.

The second advantage is that it is light and soft. A cotton-padded jacket made too thick will be too heavy to bear; made too thin, it will have no warmth at all; and after wearing it for one or two years, the cotton will be pressed as hard as a board, making it cold and uncomfortable to wear. Wool yarn has none of these drawbacks, which is another major reason for its popularity.

Wool yarn has such a need in the family, but unfortunately the market is full of foreign goods, which is really a big leak. Fortunately, starting in the past few years, our national goods have also appeared. The earliest is the Tianjin-made Ram Brand wool yarn. For the sake of national goods, it was also popular for a time. This year, Double Hands Brand wool yarn and others have also been issued. Isn't this a good phenomenon in the national goods industry!

We almost all know that the manufacture of wool yarn uses processed wool and plant fibers. If there is more wool and less fiber, then the finished product is soft and strong, meeting the standard of excellence; otherwise, it will be rough and hard, and lose hair, which is not welcomed. The Bee Brand in foreign goods meets this excellent standard, so everyone likes to use it, and it is still a force to be reckoned with! The price of domestically produced wool yarn is of course cheaper; but we must also pay attention to softness and firmness, so that it will not be defeated by foreign goods!

The Bleaching Method of Rice Straw Pulp (10) 193

— Tian Xu Wo Sheng

Making paper from rice straw was originally an ancient Chinese method. The bleaching process completely utilized sun exposure, called "native sun-drying," and did not require any chemicals. Today, using sulfite for bleaching is called "semi-sun-drying." If the color is desired to be pure white, it must be repeated several times, but it is easy to waste and disappear, which is not cost-effective. Manufacturing newsprint is sufficient with just this. Otherwise, the semi-sun-dried product should be boiled and exposed to sunlight in the open field for a long time. After being fully exposed to sunlight for a long time, its color will also turn white, which saves half the effort compared to native sun-drying, so it is called "semi-sun-drying." However, there are points to pay attention to in the bleaching process of making semi-sun-dried products, which I will explain in detail.

Rice straw pulp made with lime must first be soaked in a 1-degree hydrochloric acid solution to dissolve the lime into soluble calcium chloride, which can then be washed away. Otherwise, the lime will be covered on the outside, costing a lot of bleaching material, which is not cost-effective. When using sodium sulfite to bleach, it should first be dissolved into a 0.5% solution, and then the straw pulp that has passed through hydrochloric acid should be immersed in it for about three or four hours and taken out, and then immersed in a 1-degree hydrochloric acid solution. At this time, the above-mentioned amounts of the two solutions are only the maximum values. In fact, they are all added to the beater, which contains a lot of water, and it is impossible to accurately determine their weight. Therefore, it is like cooking, entirely dependent on the operator's experience to observe in large quantities and use appropriately. This is the same as a doctor prescribing medicine. It is absolutely impossible to copy a prescription from a medical book. Whether the doctor is skilled or not lies in this. However, if the amount of medicine used exceeds the maximum, even if the effect is immediately visible, it will definitely cause a lot of loss to the body. If it is insufficient, then its effect will be too weak, and it cannot be achieved with one dose. The effective components contained in the medicine used are also quite relevant. Even the length of heating and tapping time is very different from the loss of the finished product. Therefore, in the initial trial, there is often 100 jin of pulp, but the finished product is only half, or even as little as one-third. This is no different from cooking meat. If it is overcooked, it will definitely rot and turn into porridge. Even if it completely disappears, it is possible and not surprising.

The above method is all for newsprint purposes, and it is cheap. If you want to make fine paper that will remain white and unchanged forever, then you should use "sodium hypochlorite" to bleach, which is the most cost-effective. Its equation is Nacioh, which is to electrolyze table salt, release one part of the light, and become "sodium green oxygen light," which is commonly known as bleach. Its effect is equivalent to "peroxygen light," so it can never change color, and the cost is low.

I had a conversation with Mr. Jin and Mr. Zhu for only a dozen minutes. Although Mr. Jin took notes based on my oral description, the points to pay attention to in the bleaching process were not described in detail. Therefore, I will explain it in detail as above. Minfeng has two factories, one in Jiaxing and one in Hangzhou. Recently, because the supply of yellow cardboard has exceeded demand, they are focusing on the production of white cardboard. The original white material is quite expensive. If straw pulp can be bleached, then in addition to self-use, it can be expanded and supplied to other factories. Anyone with a flat screen machine can make newsprint. In the past, the raw material problem could not be solved, so wood pulp was purchased, and its price was actually equal to cloth pulp. Not only was there no profit to be made, but also losses had to be covered. Making grass pulp by oneself would be too busy to experiment, and experimentation is definitely not something that can be successful and satisfactory at once, so one dares not to try lightly. The factory that has tried and succeeded at the expense of sacrifice, but it is a round screen machine that can only make single-sided glossy paper, and the drying cylinder is only 72 inches, so it is not cost-effective, and there is only one cooking ball, just like cooking rice in a small pot, which cannot handle a big meal. If Minfeng can adopt straw pulp, then there will definitely be no shortage of successors. The by-products of rural areas are not just rice straw, so they can be turned into money as much as possible, and firewood can be collected for cooking. After a year, they will follow suit and become a trend. Then, money will be produced all over the countryside, turning poverty into wealth, without having to wait for ten years for trees or a hundred years for people. I really look forward to Minfeng.

Talking About Honorary Degrees and National Goods Inventors 194

— Chen Zunyuan

Last month, Fudan University held a grand celebration of its 30th anniversary. At the same time, honorary doctorates were awarded to six people, including Sun Ke. Honorary master's and honorary bachelor's degrees were also awarded to a total of ten or more people. This is indeed a major event that attracts attention, but whether the university has the right to grant these honorary degrees or whether they should be granted by the state, I do not want to discuss here. What I want to talk about now is who should be awarded honorary degrees, in other words, what kind of talent can qualify for an honorary degree.

The history of honorary degrees in China did not start today. Recalling the early years of the Republic of China, when Xu Shichang was the president of the Beijing government, the University of Paris in France had already awarded him a doctorate in literature. A few years ago, the famous performer Mei Lanfang traveled to the New World, and Pomona College in the United States also awarded him a doctorate in literature. These are all precedents for foreigners awarding honorary degrees to Chinese people. Speaking of China itself, Shanghai's St. John's University has also awarded honorary degrees to people of reputation in the country. In fact, they, the recipients of these honorary degrees, are either important figures in politics or famous people in society. People like Xu and Sun are highly respected as presidents and deans. Their reputations have long been known throughout the country. Why bother those universities to give them these degrees? If it is thought that they have merits in politics and society, then the government should grant them medals and grades to give them corresponding rewards. Why is it necessary to abuse these degrees, which are specially intended to reward those who have made special contributions to culture and academics, and send them to those noble presidents and ministers' political views or those famous social figures? This inevitably tarnishes the value of the degrees. Moreover, what China should reward today is not the political views of those noble presidents and ministers, nor the social celebrities, but the scientists who are engaged in material construction and are tireless, so the state must encourage the inventors of material production, especially the inventors of national goods, with all its energy. However, in fact, I have never heard of a national goods inventor receiving an honorary degree.

Perhaps some people will doubt why national goods inventors deserve such a reward?

This is easy to answer. National goods inventors are often able to make special discoveries in technology or machinery. It can be said that they have made considerable contributions to production, academics, and culture. Who else should be encouraged if not them? On the other hand, the materials they invent certainly bring many benefits to the country. The most obvious is that they can resist foreign goods, reduce trade deficits, eliminate waste, and increase the country's wealth. They also make great contributions to the national economy. Anyone who understands the principles of economics will know. Secondly, the relief of rural areas is currently the right medicine for the disease. Based on this, I believe that honorary degrees should be used entirely to reward inventors related to national production. That is to say, only national goods inventors are qualified to receive honorary degrees. In this way, honorary degrees have considerable regulations, and the qualifications of the recipients also have strict restrictions. Then, the dignity and preciousness of honorary degrees will not be lost.

Chunqiu

In Memory of Mr. Ge Gongzhen 196

— Zhou Shoujuan

Old friend Gongzhen, we have been apart for three years. The setting moon and lingering clouds, how can I not think of you? Sometimes, new geese pass by my small building, bringing a letter. Opening it and reading it repeatedly, the emotions are evident in the words. The tiny characters, clear and sparse, are like seeing the face of an old friend. However, with ten thousand miles separating us, it is difficult to pour out accumulated feelings. I can only wish him well for the country's sake. Last winter, Zhou Zijianyun and his wife and Ms. Hu Die traveled to Soviet Russia. I entrusted them with a small note to express my feelings. Soon, I received his reply, along with a colored portrait of the Russian literary master Gorky. The letter said:

Brother Shoujuan: Brother Jianyun came and brought your letter. I am delighted to know that your writings are better than ever, and I am even more envious of your peaceful life in Keli. I have been wandering overseas in recent years and am tired and homesick. However, Brother Jianyun will arrive in Shanghai before me. There is no need to elaborate on the situation here. I will go to Berlin the day after tomorrow for a short rest. I wrote a note at the beginning of the year to offer New Year's greetings. The Gorky portrait was accidentally inserted into the book. It has been a long time and I have not sent it. Now I am sending it with this letter, knowing that someone overseas misses you. I wish you and your wife peace. Your brother, Gongzhen. April 25th.

I was overjoyed to receive the letter and treasured it carefully. When Brother Jianyun returned, we talked about overseas affairs. He first mentioned Gongzhen, describing his diligent and studious nature. I was ashamed of my own decline and admired him even more. This time, Gongzhen returned from his travels, but I did not have a chance to see him. I was depressed due to commercial setbacks and losses. My old friends Xiaodie and Fuchao strongly invited me to travel to Huangshan to forget my worries. On the way back, on the train to Jixi, I read the Southeast Daily and suddenly learned the news of Gongzhen's death. I was shocked and could not calm down. The heavens have taken away my relatives and friends in recent years, and I can no longer count them. Anger accumulated in my heart, and I wanted to point to the sky and scold it. I did not expect the devastation to be endless, and now it has taken Gongzhen away from me! Alas, Gongzhen, I wanted to learn from you when you returned, but I thought there would be plenty of time and there was no need to rush to see you. I thought we could talk freely. Who knew that your return to your homeland seemed to be solely for the purpose of returning to your ancestral grave. In the blink of an eye, you suddenly passed away. Is it because you loved your country so much that you longed for this unfortunate homeland and wanted to bury your bones in this remnant of a mountain? Alas, Gongzhen, you are gone now. In this autumn of great difficulty for all parties, it is not unfortunate for you. How can the survivors bear the pain of losing a good friend! If your soul is conscious, how will it comfort me?

News of Wu Music (Qin) 197

— Lu Hua

In recent years, dance halls and singing pavilions, and foreign music have flourished, and nothing can be compared with them to please the ears and hearts. As for the art of the qin, it has almost become a lost art. The so-called noble hermits, playing Shang and Ke Yu, are just decorations for poetry, lyrics, and songs. This autumn, on the ninth day of the ninth month, Mr. Chengjiang Zhuang Jiancheng, a man of refined taste and soaring enthusiasm, invited qin friends from various provinces such as Fujian, Hunan, Anhui, Hubei, Sichuan, and Yue to meet at Gu's Yiyuan Garden. That morning, those who walked on the road to Hulong Road saw people passing by with qins, and those who did not know the matter pointed to it as Japanese people holding a qin meeting in a certain garden. (The qin and chess are both inherent arts of our country. Now, the seat of chess has been ceded to the Japanese, and the art of the qin will also be given to the Japanese? This is a small matter, but it is enough to show the psychology of the Chinese people.) Those who played the qin in the meeting were Li Zizhao, Wu Lansun, Guo Tongfu, Peng Ziqing, Zha Fuxi, Wu Xiangquan, Wu Xiangcen, Wu Xiangheng, and Zhuang Jiancheng. Li was 79 years old, the oldest, and Ms. Xiangcen and Xiangheng were the youngest, both under the age of twenty. Mr. Zha Fuxi was Zhuang's teacher. Zha said to people: Jiancheng is my disciple in the inner chamber. Jiancheng told me: He learned the qin from his teacher, not just the manipulation of the strings. He has discovered subtleties in the distinction of rhythm that have not been discovered by predecessors. He also said that rhythm is a rule, and sound is a natural sound. Today's performers often confine the natural sound to the rules of rhythm. This is the ability to excel in the art of playing the qin, but not enough to speak of the ultimate way of qin music. Zha played a song of Xiaoxiang Water and Clouds, a total of eighteen sections, written by Guo Chu of the Song Dynasty, whose laws belong to the one without shooting. The first three sections are harmonious and slow, so that the listener can see the misty state of the clouds and mountains and the hazy trees. The fourth section and below are soothing and expansive, leading people's minds to meet, like a boat traveling among the clouds and water. The most wonderful thing is that when the performance reaches the end, those who listen around are still leaning on the table, leaning on the machine, and leaning on the pillars as before. This is to restrain the inner and quiet the outer? Jiancheng played Changmen Yuan, expressing the grievance in the word Yuan, which cannot be said to be out of the blue, but it is different from the performance of the qin workers in the past. The other performances by Li and the others were all perfect. Mr. Zha took a picture of the meeting and dispersed. The owner of the garden, Mr. Yanping, said: In the autumn of the ninth year of the Republic, Mr. Ye Zhangbo of Hangzhou also held a grand qin meeting in this place. Dozens of people attended, and there were two monks and no women playing the qin. It is not impossible to say that today's meeting is better than the meeting in the past.

Feng Feng 198

— Xin Yi

I have never been willing to flatter people in my life, and I am especially afraid of talking about cheesy things, so writing this article is definitely not flattering Feng Feng, but recording Feng Feng. Here, I must first make a statement.

Speaking of the words "Feng Feng", most friends who like to watch singing and dancing will feel a little flushed, and they all know that she is good at performing flirtatious plays, and there is an unspeakable heat on the stage that will strongly burn the audience's heart. Anyone who has seen her has tasted that unspeakable taste. Therefore, in the ideals of ordinary people, she must be a romantic urban lady; otherwise, how can she be so profound on the stage?

However, unexpected things are not without exception. When she leaves the stage, you will never believe that she is the "Feng Feng" on the stage. You must say that she is a big country girl; originally, a set of blue cloth short jacket and pants, a pair of cloth-soled ten shoes, when she returns home, she does needlework, washes rice and vegetables, sweeps the floor and wipes the table, everything is done, and she still blushes when she sees strangers. Where is she like a fashionable singing and dancing star.

Her family is very poor. In addition to her parents, she also has a young brother, who all need the money that she earns to support them. Therefore, although she is one of the highest paid in the troupe, she never dares to waste a penny. She is very frugal with herself. She never hires a car when she goes out, and she is reluctant to buy a snack to eat when she is hungry. Every month, she gives all the money she receives to her mother, and only keeps two eight-opening books for herself.

Finally, I should introduce that she is the pillar of the Silver Moon Troupe. She is only sixteen years old this year. She has a naturally pleasing face, which is appropriately matched with a healthy and modern physique. Moreover, she has a very deep foundation in singing and dancing, and she is still diligently moving forward, which is incomparable with the current group of so-called stars who only know how to flirt and have no real talent. Because I feel that whether it is drama, movies, or singing and dancing, she is a very promising talent, so I am happy to record the above.

Little Western Paradise 199

— Written by Zhang Huaishui

Chapter Twenty: Struggling to Live, Seeing the Beloved Grandson, Shedding Tears; Remembering the Past in a Year of Famine, Sowing Wheat Bringing Disaster

Only then did that military officer come out, still holding a whip in his hand. He glared and shouted, "What are you crying about? I haven't even used the whip to beat them, that's already letting them off easy. Tell you honestly, if you don't hand over the grain, I won't let them down." That family knelt on the ground, and there was a man who was a bit smarter than us. He said that the family really didn't have any grain, and they had always lived on grass roots. Unless they waited for the newly planted wheat in our fields to be harvested, they could hand it over then. That military officer had never shown a smile to us, but upon hearing this, his face suddenly brightened up and he smiled. He pointed at us with the whip and said, "You said this yourself. Can you provide a guarantee?" We originally didn't know what "providing a guarantee" meant. Later, the military officer said, "Providing a guarantee means writing a note." We couldn't write, so he could write it for us. Once it was written, we just needed to put a fingerprint on it. This wasn't difficult, so we agreed. He immediately took out a piece of paper, let down the people who were hanging, called the soldiers to bring an inkstone, grabbed a person's finger, pressed it in the inkstone, and then pressed it on the paper. He said it was all done, and released my father. But my father couldn't walk on his own; the people from the fortress carried him back. We were all fools, thinking that this meant the big problem was over. My father slept for a night, recovered his breath, and, thinking about the wheat in the field that could be harvested in a day or two, got up early to check on it. Unexpectedly, that piece of land's wheat had already been completely harvested. Several soldiers, carrying bundles of wheat, were carrying them away on shoulder poles. My father... my father..." He choked up at this point. (353)

Record of Lingering Fragrance 200

— Originally written by Princess Der Ling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

"Nonsense!" After a while, she struggled to say, "Don't talk nonsense! This is clearly a terrible omen. Who are you trying to deceive? You clearly know it's an omen, so why are you turning it upside down and saying the opposite? Do you think I don't know? Hmph! Only a three-year-old child would take it as a good omen!"

Although the Empress Dowager said these few words very softly, her tone was very angry and intense. After speaking, she fiercely waved her right hand outward, meaning to tell Li Lianying to leave immediately. Li Lianying couldn't have been happier to do so, so as to avoid being scolded unnecessarily, and hurriedly kowtowed and went out.

Then the Empress Dowager turned around and said to me:

"Don't laugh at us for being timid! This flower does have a somewhat eerie aura. Perhaps some disaster is about to befall us, or our country!" She said to me in a whisper; her attitude was still very solemn, and her eyebrows were almost knitted together.

At that time, listening to her say that so softly, I gradually began to believe it too. I myself absolutely did not believe in any good or bad omens, and her words could not change my belief. It was only because I had followed her for so many days that I had deeply experienced how great the power she possessed was. Since she already possessed such great power and was so deeply superstitious about good and bad omens, wasn't it possible that she herself would create a disaster because of that magnolia flower? Therefore, the Empress Dowager was worried about a disaster because of her superstition about omens, and I was worried that a disaster would really occur because of my belief in her power. Although we were both worried, our psychology was different. (449)

World Oddities

Roscoe's Private Life 201

— Qing

Since the American slapstick star Roscoe gave us a rather bad impression with his film "Never Say Die," his works have not come to China for a long time. Perhaps he is taking a full rest these past few years and doesn't have any new works? But Roscoe's past achievements are still unforgettable to us. Now I will talk about his private life as a topic of conversation after tea and dinner.

Roscoe's real name is Harold Lloyd. He is a simple and modest person. His wife, Mildred Davis, was the female lead in many of his previous films. They have been married for many years and are still as loving as ever, and they already have very cute children. In the films, he always wears black-rimmed glasses, but as soon as he leaves the studio, he takes off his glasses. He never wears glasses in his daily life. He likes to work, loves fame, and loves money, but he especially loves his family. Except for work, he puts all his energy into his wife and children.

He has starred in 350 films and earned a lot of money, making him one of the richest stars in Hollywood. However, he is very thrifty and invests wisely in various businesses, never failing. He was very poor before, so he knows that money doesn't come easily, so he never wastes it. His greatest luxury is his house, which has a twenty-acre garden and a swimming pool and a golf course. The house is large and magnificent, decorated to the utmost beauty, truly like a palace from a myth. Just because the house and garden are so large, he has to hire many servants, so he has eighteen gardeners, a chauffeur, and more than ten male and female servants. Seeing that he has so many servants, you would think he is very extravagant. But in fact, he is very shrewd. If the meat delivered from the butcher shop is a little short, he will protest. He also knows exactly how many eggs his family eats. All the bills are managed by a secretary, but he checks them himself every month. If there are any discrepancies, he will definitely ask about them in detail. He pays all the bills every month and never delays, even if it's just a penny or two. He also records them. If the prices of food and other daily necessities change and differ from the bills, he must know the reason. Roscoe himself stipulates a weekly allowance of one hundred gold dollars and never exceeds this amount. There are also regulations for the expenses of his wife and children.

Roscoe likes a quiet life and never holds grand banquets. He is never seen in the extravagant social circles of Hollywood. But he never participates in gambling, boat races, or polo either. His wife is as simple as he is and does not care about dressing up. She does not associate with the fashionable female stars of Hollywood but quietly lives her peaceful family life. Roscoe's family all love flowers, but they are not willing to spend too much money. The flowers they use are all grown in their own garden, and sometimes they buy a batch from the flower shop wholesale, which is very cheap. When they entertain relatives and friends, they just eat a simple meal, chat for a while, or play a game of mahjong without betting, and that's how they spend an evening. Roscoe and his wife often play tennis and golf as their daily exercise. Every summer, Roscoe's wife and children often wear swimsuits and swim in the swimming pool.

Their children, a son named Harold Jr., and a daughter named Gloria, also have a foster daughter named Punchy, who are all well-behaved and docile children. Roscoe's wife often gives them strict family education and does not let up. They each have a fixed amount of allowance every month. If they want to buy new toys but have already spent their allowance for the month, they have to wait until next month to buy them, and there is no flexibility. Although the two daughters are young, Roscoe's wife has already taught them sewing and cooking, and also has them make their beds, to make them useful citizens in the future. They usually call their mother "Med," which is different from calling her "Mama." But Med is now completely different from when she played the female lead in her husband's films. Her golden hair and blue eyes have not changed, but she has become a sophisticated and thoughtful woman. She only thinks about her husband and children, is gentle and considerate, and truly cares for them in every possible way. She is truly a model of a virtuous wife and loving mother in Hollywood.

The October Gold Rooster Yarn contract was listed on May 1st at 179.4 yuan. At this time, Shanghai was experiencing a turbulent financial crisis, with banks and money shops successively collapsing. The situation in North China was also serious, and the market gradually declined, reaching a low of 165.3 yuan on June 18th. However, yarn factories were affected by operational difficulties, with many suspending operations or reducing working hours, leading to a daily decrease in production. Marker prices rose, and rumors spread throughout the market, revisiting the issue of inflation. Furthermore, there was the organization of long-term trading companies and large-scale purchases. Market prices gradually increased, soaring by 4 yuan in one day on July 29th, reaching a high of 179.4 yuan. Unexpectedly, after the high prices, actual demand stagnated, and market sentiment turned sharply downward, breaking the 70 yuan mark. Subsequently, with the recent surge in gold prices and intense rumors about the paper money issue, coupled with the sharp decline in Shanghai's yarn inventory, market sentiment became agitated, reaching a high of 182.5 yuan. Free Talk

On the Nature of Comedy and "The Inspector General" 220

— Traveler from Okayama

Most people tend to easily misunderstand comedy (Comedy), thinking that comedy is just something that makes people laugh. However, the essence of comedy is not that simple. If the meaning of comedy is really just about making people laugh and "moving away from reality, losing its vivid content," then this kind of drama has completely lost its fundamental meaning! It has simply become a game!" (Belinsky). Therefore, Gogol fervently said: "Is theater actually manufacturing toys to coax children?!"

When the European stage of the 19th century was almost completely occupied by unrealistic melodrama and vaudeville, Gogol once protested loudly: "Melodrama and vaudeville have dominated the world of drama for five years! What an ugly sight!... If a genius with authority could sweep away this miasma, then the whole world would place him alongside Byron. This is not a humorous statement, because in this effort there is considerable comfort. Alexandre Dumas and other masters have become legislators for the whole world. I dare to swear that this is really the shame of these five years of the nineteenth century! Oh, Molière, the great Molière, it is you who have broadly developed all characters, even the shadows of characters! You, the strict, deeply thoughtful Racine, you are the one who, in the world of poetry, illuminates the value of humanity with noble enthusiasm. Please look at what is popular on our stage after you? Look, what a terrible monster—the ugliness of melodrama—is wandering among us! Where exactly are we living? Where are we, with all the modern troubles and unfathomable uncertainties? We can't even find a little reflection of ourselves in melodrama, but our melodrama is utterly unscrupulous, with nothing but lies... "

The melodrama and vaudeville of that era were completely terrifying, absurd dramas. The dialogue contained so-called satire, but it had no connection to living reality. This kind of drama turned the theater, which should be "a forum for civic education and moral instruction," into "a useless place of entertainment"! Therefore, Gogol "bitterly attacked playwrights for stuffing works with no connection to real life into the repertoire." Gogol believed that the greatest danger harming the essence of drama lies in the misinterpretation of comedic characters, that is, perceiving the characters in the play as amusing entertainment. Gogol said: "Laughter is more important and deeper than people imagine. It is by no means laughter that is provided for entertainment due to momentary stimuli and arising from an unhealthy temperament. Rather, it is laughter that bursts forth from people's honest nature... If someone does something base and trivial, and a terrifying, satirical force is displayed before him, but he pretends and shouts: 'There is no such person!' This shows that his understanding is more critical than others." This kind of healthy laughter is precisely contained in Gogol's works. From novels and dramas such as "The Inspector General," "The Overcoat," and "Dead Souls," he enables people to find some real, typical characters in real society. These characters, under his pen, become deeply recognized and familiar to everyone, perhaps those bureaucrats, local tyrants, landlords, and village chiefs who grow up around them...

Belinsky said: "Comedy is absolutely not comical, it is the same kind of thing as tragedy. In essence, comedy and tragedy are only one step apart. In the depths of comedic laughter, there also lies the secret tear that constitutes the power of tragedy. This laughter arises from the sharp insight into everything decadent, base, and that destroys humanity. Because the humor of the licentious will eventually fall into ruin and depression. If this kind of depression does not exist for people, then comedy will not exist either. That kind of vulgar teasing, that kind of laughter that loses its true content, and the clown's nonsense are all not comedy. True comedy contains the same noble meaning as tragedy, and occupies an equal position and value in the theatrical world. Comedy is not a farce that uses stupid things to please the audience. Like tragedy, it is the mysterious posture of human nature, the cry of humanity." This passage provides a concise and essential explanation of the nature of comedy. And Gogol and his drama permeate from this "secret tear." His "Inspector General" exposes the general incompetence and flattery of bureaucrats. Belinsky said: "This comedy contains a very deep observation of real society, and laughter that bursts forth from the heart." Moreover, "due to these two forces, it can give people an unprecedentedly profound impression. For this reason, the appearance of Gogol's "Inspector General" received severe attacks from the conservative society at the time. However, these attacks still could not destroy the extremely important role of Gogol's realistic satirical works in Russian literature. They left a magnificent impact in the Nicholas Dynasty of the nineteenth century, laying a solid foundation for realism in Russia.

The appearance of "The Inspector General" made people recognize Gogol's great genius for drama. He, like Molière, "began his career as a comedic writer with laughter full of boisterous, healthy joy." Molière "overcame farce and burlesque with comedies of social psychology, thereby creating comedic types corresponding to his own class, and thus also creating comedic types that could serve as models for civic comedies in other countries" (Fritz Mauthner). Gogol developed a great affection for Molière, but his "Inspector General" was completed under the encouragement of Pushkin. However, he did not go so far as to say, as was mistakenly rumored outside, that "Pushkin told him this story" (Li Zegang: "European Modern Literature," page 205). Because from Gogol's keen observation, his loyalty to objective realism is not surprising. Regarding Gogol's works, as Pushkin said, "Gogol didn't fabricate anything. This is pure truth, terrible truth!" This "terrible truth" is even "superior to Pushkin" (Belinsky).

Due to dissatisfaction with the initial performance of "The Inspector General" on stage, a fundamental struggle arose between Gogol and the theater. Gogol said: "The performance of "The Inspector General" was actually performed as something crude, simply unlike my work. The protagonist was a complete failure. [Actor Dür] who played the protagonist) did not understand even a hair of what Khlestakov ("The Inspector General"'s protagonist) was like. He actually played Khlestakov as a clown or a rogue who seemed to have come from a Parisian theater, wearing clothes from the second century and wearing makeup..." As a result of this struggle, Gogol won, so that: "In order to be able to fully unfold the rich content of that script to the audience, it was immediately felt that the theater and the actors needed a new and special attitude." Because actors accustomed to the vaudeville style would not understand the essence of comedy... After this, Gogol caused a qualitative change in the Russian theatrical world.

Regardless of how much religious mysticism Gogol's later years contained in discussions of drama, his "Inspector General" becoming the most brilliant play of nineteenth-century Russian drama is undeniable. Belinsky said: "Since Gogol's play appeared, one cannot read a better script or see a better performance." This is not an exaggeration.

By the Golden Thread Spring 221

— Zhang Chunqiao

I lived in Jinan for four or five years, almost entirely in poverty and busyness. Because of poverty, I had to be busy; the result of being busy was still poverty. In autumn, people were clamoring to go to Longdong to see the red leaves, and I myself was very willing to go and have some fun. Although I am a vulgar person, everyone needs entertainment. However, running there is impossible; the road is too far. Taking a car there is impossible; I don't have the money for a car. As a result, I went to Golden Thread Spring with a friend.

Golden Thread Spring, to the east of Baotu Spring, has a large gate with a plaque that says "Shangshu Hall." Going through this gate, you can find it. Inside the gate is a small courtyard. Through another gate is a drill ground. The sound of the windmill turning creaks rhythmically, often drowning out the noisy shouts. On the west side of the courtyard, there is a small garden.

The three of us entered the small garden. The cool autumn wind shook the leaves, shaking our sleeves. It was indeed desolate. It no longer had its former abundance, that fresh abundance.

There were not many people. In the middle of the courtyard, there is a water pavilion. It is surrounded by clear water. All this water flows from the northwest corner of the courtyard. That source is the Golden Thread Spring. The water flowing from the Golden Thread Spring mixes with the slow flow of the Jade Gargling Pool opposite and flows outside the wall.

The three of us sat on the rocks of the artificial mountain.

Tall trees, their branches and leaves intricately intertwined in the sky, made it impossible to see the high heavens of the north. I remember that in summer, the leaves were even denser. In spring, the fragrance of flowers and the songs of birds intoxicated the people of spring even more. Now, autumn has arrived, the season of "poets" has arrived. Some are going to Hangzhou to watch the tide, some are admiring the red leaves, some are suffering even more, and some are stealing even more leisure. In the grass pavilion in the southwest corner of the courtyard, two old men in their fifties or sixties were playing chess. We, too, were resting leisurely.

Staring at the pool of emerald green water, the "poet" inscribed poetic lines in his shorthand notebook. I don't remember it clearly, but it was probably describing this winding stream. He said that the water was as green as solidified grape juice, and it must be as sweet as rock candy. And the turning over of the fish in the water, he thought, was even more beautiful, so beautiful that he didn't have the right words to describe it. Another friend, Feng, was planning a painting. As for me, I had an indescribable taste, flooding like a tide in my heart.

On the bank of the pool, there were two tall banana trees. The fat, green leaves were still growing vigorously.

None of us had seen the golden thread connected to the Golden Thread Spring. I have also heard people say that it is easy to see in the morning and evening. The three of us did not encounter this opportunity. Then, we talked about the Jade Gargling Liquid. The Jade Gargling Pool was ordinary and had nothing to see. However, I heard that the Jade Gargling Pool was the former residence of the lyricist Li Qingzhao, and her famous Jade Gargling Lyrics were written here.

I don't know how many people like the Jade Gargling Lyrics, but the Jade Gargling Pool is dilapidated, like its owner, leaving only a name in history.

—Damn it, let's also make a pool and write a collection of poems!

—Damn it, let's also make a pool and create a painting!

The two of them ridiculed each other, writing black words and black lines in their notebooks with their pencils, muttering as if they didn't want anyone to hear, but also wanted people to hear. They constantly shook, measuring angles, and thinking about words. I looked at the two of them boredly and said:

—Let's scatter, folks. The poems written in this place can only decorate bookshelves. The paintings created in this place can only decorate living rooms. Let's say less!

The "poet" glared at me and said:

—You rest. You have to work tomorrow!

Lasting Peace 222

— Written by Huang Shiying

A Couple (Two) 223

— Bai Chen

The ticket seller's eyes darted around, staring at the man. "Where to?"

The man took out the counted copper coins, "Great [Da] Ma Road, two tickets."

The woman glanced at the man, not responding.

"Gu..."

"Mud City Bridge...!"

A rush of people surged on. In the middle was a friend carrying a small leather suitcase, who rushed to the glass door and stopped. Opening the suitcase, he took out several packages of candy. He opened his mouth and shouted:

"Hey, gentlemen! Anyone want to eat cream chocolate candy? This is produced by Shanghai Dahua Candy Company. Due to the new opening to promote business, it is a special discount. Good stuff, cheap price, real cream chocolate, usually selling for two dimes a piece, today only selling for two cents. And buy five get one free. Two cents buys six candies..."

Several people turned to look at the road. Several people looked at the moving mouth.

The friend carrying the small suitcase was not embarrassed at all by the people who ignored him. He kept saying: "Gentlemen, want to try it? I have samples here..." He reached into the suitcase and pulled out many small paper packages.

The woman looked at the man, who curled his lip. "Advertising!" He turned away.

The small paper packages were distributed to the opposite side, "Everyone, please try it. It doesn't matter. The samples don't cost money. If you like it, please take care of my business."

Some of the opposite guests took them, some shook their heads.

"Try it, try it, gentlemen!" He said in a very polite voice, but his face was like carved wood.

The small paper packages came to this side. The woman glanced sideways. The man also glanced at it, half of his face still facing the window.

"Sir, try it..."

The first person shook his head. The second person also shook his head. The third person was naturally embarrassed not to shake his head. The fourth person—the man followed suit, and the woman quickly followed the man's lead.

"It doesn't matter, try it. It doesn't matter if you don't buy it."

That guy was really thick-skinned. Even though people shook their heads, he still threw the small paper packages at people—one package per person.

The man glared at the guy as if angrily. The woman secretly looked at the man.

The man's eyes were looking out the window, his left hand lightly touching the small paper package, then pinching and weighing it between his three fingers, not even looking at it. The woman followed the man's lead, but put it in the folds of her handkerchief.

"Which gentleman will take care of my business?..."

That guy stared at the woman. The woman turned to stare at the man. "Want to buy it for the child...?"

The man shook his head annoyedly, "No!" With a wave of his left hand, the paper package was taken into the palm of his hand.

The woman lowered her head and didn't speak.

The guy carrying the small suitcase put the candy back into the suitcase, closed it, and went to the other side. Silently, like a passenger on the bus.

Several people seemed to breathe a sigh of relief. The small third class was calm.

The man put his left hand and right hand together, with the back of his hand facing up, doing something. There was a slight sound of tearing paper. His eyes were looking at the opposite guest, and his left hand was brought to his mouth.

The woman turned her face to look, and the man's mouth was moving a little.

The woman understood and straightened her handkerchief. Slowly opening the small paper package, she stole a glance and saw a purplish-black thing. "Oh!... This is..." she thought.

Seeing two guests across the way also moving their mouths, she mustered up her courage: "I can't be wrong!" So her mouth moved slightly as well.

But who was that? Standing at the door was that guy carrying the small suitcase. With bulging eyes, he stared at her.

Her face turned red, and she lowered her head, tightly closing her mouth.

"Gu..."

The man nudged her with his elbow. "Get off."

Getting off the tram, she looked around and found that they had already crossed the Great Ma Road. She asked, "Where is this...?" It was only now that she thought of the candy in her mouth.

"Fourth Ma Road!"

"Ptooey!" She spat out a mouthful of saliva, red and red. "This kind of candy is bitter!" (The End)

This newspaper's weekly "Women's Garden" will no longer be published from November. Shenbao [Shanghai Newspaper] Supplement

Talking

Thoughts on Holding a Visiting Group for Suffering Children 225

— Mengruo

Everyone knows that with the holding of China's Children's Year, the children who enjoy happiness are limited to children from middle-class and above families. As for the children of most poor families, they are still excluded. You see, every time there is a children's gathering, those who act as children's representatives or dance the Grape Fairy on stage are always little brothers and sisters wearing beautiful new clothes. There are very few ragged suffering children. Of course, we cannot say that the people in charge do not allow these suffering children to participate, but because the suffering children do not have the opportunity to join in the fun.

This time, however, it is an exception. Suffering children also get to enjoy the happiness of Children's Year. Recently, the Municipal Children's Year Implementation Committee held a visiting group for suffering children, wanting to travel to Kunshan. Participants are limited to suffering children raised by various charitable organizations in Shanghai. It is expected that there will be eighty people from the Shanghai Orphanage, eighty people from the Jiangwan Ciyou Sanatorium of the China Relief and Mutual Aid Association, sixty people from the Poor People's Training Institute, sixty people from the Ciyou Training Institute of the Chinese Ciyou Association, and twenty people from the Huier Orphanage of the Zhabei Charitable Group. The purpose of the visit is Kunshan, traveling back and forth by Jinghu [Beijing-Shanghai] Railway train. The places to visit are Ma'anshan [Saddle Mountain], Public Sports Ground, Kunshan Park, Kunshan Farm, Huancheng [Circumferential] Road, and various suffering children's care institutions. It is also planned to hold a banquet for suffering children at the foot of Ma'anshan Mountain, with officials from the association and local party and government leaders participating and giving speeches. This move is not considered to be particularly beneficial to suffering children, but the significance is very good. At least it can express a little of the spirit of Children's Year, on the one hand, to make these three hundred suffering children who participate in the visiting group realize that they also have the right to enjoy the happiness of Children's Year, and on the other hand, to make the general public not dare to ignore the status of suffering children.

However, Children's Year has a greater responsibility for suffering children than this. Children's Year is Children's Year for all children in the country, not Children's Year for a small number of special-class children. The happiness that Children's Year bestows on suffering children should not be superficial, but real happiness. One trip is just giving them an opportunity for entertainment. How to improve their lives is what we must care about. Therefore, in the future, Children's Year's work should take on the heavy responsibility of education and upbringing for suffering children. Children belong to society and the country. Poor families do not have the ability to educate and raise children, so society must educate and raise them. We cannot forget them just because they are born poor. Suffering children are also the masters of the country, and the fate of the future country is placed on them.

Pacing 226

— Huazhi

After dinner, the child began to doze off by the table. Because he had eaten too much, I took his hand and asked him to learn from me and pace in the room. He leaned against me, walking slowly, while rubbing his sleepy eyelids with his other hand, looking so reluctant and unhappy. But after walking back and forth four or five times, his sleepiness ran away, so he threw off my hand and turned around mischievously, pacing with a full air, like a clown. Seeing this, my wife smiled and said to me, "He has learned your worried look. It's a pity he can't frown and stare at people with a terrible look. Otherwise, it would be exactly the same!"

I stopped like that, watching the child pacing. Usually, when I am surrounded by unresolved matters, I always turn my hands and pace; this has become a habit. But I can't see my own clownish appearance, swaying and swaying; the child sees it, and as soon as he has the opportunity to develop, he immediately imitates that appearance. I didn't want to leave this stain on his pure and bright heart, so I sternly scolded him, not allowing him to turn his hands over, not allowing him to sway like a clown. Although he cried, and my wife also blamed me for scolding him unreasonably, I felt relieved, as if I had saved a person; and I urged myself not to make that strange appearance again as an example to the child.

Of course, I wouldn't create that kind of appearance myself. I was infected by my father—this is not knowledge, not property. I want to get rid of this bad habit from my child's generation. This habit is not only "ugly," but also a depiction of my father's lifelong frustration. He died so depressed.

My father was an old scholar, who did not pass the imperial examination, which was his lifelong regret. Every time he failed and returned home, he would lock himself in the study, not allowing family members to enter, and not coming out himself, neglecting sleep and food to desperately study. My father was a learned man, and my grandmother loved him very much. Every time he had a fit of bookishness, only my grandmother could dissuade him. According to my grandmother, my father's appearance at that time was beautiful, hanging a book, swaying back and forth in the study, simply like a fool. At that time, my older brother was only two years old, and I was still in swaddling clothes, so of course I didn't see my father pacing. Even when my grandmother described that situation, we were still young. Seeing my grandmother laugh, we also laughed. We still couldn't guess an accurate picture of pacing. I witnessed my father pacing like a clown when my brother and I went to university—since the Qing Dynasty was overthrown and the imperial examination was abolished, my father decided to give up studying and go into business. However, it is so difficult for a scholar with a bookish air to share food with the cunning and deceitful merchants. And my father still valued reading so much that he insisted that we graduate from university. Since doing business failed, paying for our brothers' tuition became stretched; I witnessed my father pacing at this time. He locked his brows, turned his hands back, swayed back and forth, sometimes smoking cigarettes, not knowing that the end of the cigarette had burned his fingernails. Seeing my father's anxious state of being unable to cope, and not being able to share his worries, I followed my father and started pacing. The last time was when the manager of the store absconded, and we were forced to a dead end by the creditors. My father and I paced in the store all night; due to this change, my father died in depression. The image of that night cannot be erased from my memory. This pacing became a habit. The child saw it, and he paced the same way. I thought of my father's lifelong frustration and depression, and I was taking over my father's fate. Seeing the child pacing, I couldn't help but worry that this child was a third-generation victim!

International Balloon Race Record 227

— Shui Quan

The Gordon Bennett Cup International Balloon Race has been held for decades and is of great interest to the aviation community. The large silver cup was donated by the late American Gordon Bennett, hence the name. It was founded in 1894 and is held annually. Representatives from various countries participate, but only balloons manufactured in their own country are eligible. The criteria for winning are based on the balloon's ascent altitude, landing distance, and time spent in the air. The rules stipulate that any country that wins three consecutive years will permanently retain the cup. Since the competition began, various countries have had wins and losses. The United States had several consecutive wins twice, but was deprived of the third win by another country, which was a pity. In 1934 and 1935, Poland won the championship twice. This year was a critical juncture, and the competition was even more intense. As a result, Poland won again, winning three consecutive times, and thus permanently retained the cup. The Polish government prepared a new silver cup, and the competition will continue to be held from next year, with all rules remaining the same.

Seven countries participated. According to the rules, the competition venue should be held in the capital of the country that won the previous year. Therefore, this year's competition was held in Warsaw, the capital of Poland, on September 15. Seven countries participated, namely the United States, France, Germany, Belgium, New Zealand, Poland, and Switzerland. The venue was at the airfield. On that day, the President of Poland, Mościcki, ministers of various departments, and military attachés from various countries' embassies in Poland all attended to watch the competition. More than 100,000 people rushed to the event, which was very lively. The opening ceremony was held at 3:00 PM, and the President gave a speech. The competition began at 4:00 PM.

Thirteen balloons. A total of thirteen balloons participated in the competition. The exteriors were painted in various colors, bright and beautiful. Before taking off, each crew member made a three-minute radio broadcast speech. At exactly 4:00 PM, the first balloon ascended into the sky. Before long, the thirteen balloons took off one after another, floating in the air, flying farther and farther, as small as shooting stars, vaguely disappearing into the distance. At that time, military music played loudly, and the audience gradually dispersed.

Landing in Russian territory. The results of the competition were as follows: the first place was won by the Polonia balloon, piloted by Polish Colonel Panseński and his assistant Wisłocki, with a landing distance of more than 1,600 kilometers and an altitude of more than 1,000 miles, landing in the Volga River in Russian territory. The second place was also won by a Polish balloon named Warsaw, with a distance of 1,500 kilometers, landing near Mequisk in Russian territory. The third place was Belgium, the fourth place was Germany, the fifth place was Poland, the sixth place was New Zealand, the seventh place was France, the eighth place was also France, the ninth place was Belgium, the tenth place was Switzerland, the eleventh place was Germany, the twelfth place was Germany, and the American balloon Navy was last.

Prizes for the winners. In addition to the silver cup, the winners of the balloon race also receive cash prizes. The first place receives 10,000 Polish złoty, the second place 7,000 Polish złoty, the third place 4,000 Polish złoty, and the subsequent places receive 2,500, 1,500, 1,200, 1,000, and 800 Polish złoty respectively. The prizes were donated by Polish President Mościcki, the Minister of Communications, the Minister of Foreign Affairs, and the Minister of the Army.

Balloon Manufacturing. After Poland won three consecutive times, the Gordon Bennett Cup, which has been contested for nearly 50 years, is permanently owned by Poland, earning the highest international honor. According to observations by participants in the competition, Poland's victory is purely due to the excellence of its balloon manufacturing. It is generally believed that Poland should be the first to promote the science and sports use of balloons in the world. It is reported that Belgian scientist Professor Piccard once ascended into the stratosphere in a balloon for scientific exploration. He recently telegraphed to Warsaw, specifically ordering a new balloon for his re-exploration.

Production 228

— Qin Jian

Copper-smith Zhang Siguan has been feeling depressed lately: the shop hasn't had any work for two months, and his wife's belly is growing bigger day by day, and she's about to give birth.

Looking at the three little children! Two boys and one girl! Playing at the door, his heart trembles: he can't even feed the three he already has, what will he do with another one? In this day and age, it's a sin for poor people to have children!

But what can he do? The fourth is coming soon. Siguan and his wife are not young anymore. They like children, but in the current situation, the father's responsibility makes him tremble. Looking at the three children he already has: hungry, thin, ragged, filthy, he feels like he has committed an indelible sin, and he is always filled with painful discomfort and apology.

It's my fault, it's my fault! Your "fate" is so bad, why did you have to be born into my family?

Sometimes, walking down the street, he peeks through the iron gate of a "well-equipped" small school, looking at those lively, lovely, and happy children, and he thinks of his three wild dog-like children at home: the eldest is eight years old, and he should be going to school too, like those other children, doing morning exercises, "One, two, three, four!", singing about little sparrows, jumping and laughing; but... but his own children are left to roam the streets all day long...

Then, his heart feels like it's being stabbed with a knife, he's depressed, tormented, desperately thinking, like he's gone mad.

But the neighbors on either side keep saying those hateful words to him, which, in his opinion, are simply like thorns, endless words:

"Congratulations, Siguan, your wife is full-term, congratulations on having a fat, healthy baby boy, treat us to some red eggs."

But Siguan feels a kind of unbearable humiliation: "Congratulations my ass! Having children in this day and age! Debt collectors! I can't feed them, I might as well take it to the orphanage after it's born."

The woman gets anxious when she hears this: "What are you saying? What are you talking about? Are you crazy? Are you really...?"

"What do you know! There's no work, and you still want to give birth like a sow! I can't feed it, do you understand!"

The woman starts to cry: "You heartless bastard! What are you saying! You have the heart to take the child to the orphanage, I'll sue you, I will, I'll... fight you! You wolf in sheep's clothing...!"

However, at night, when everyone is quiet, Siguan softly says to his wife: "Zhaodi, you have to understand me this time, I'm not that kind of person, I like children too. But, there's been no work for two months, if we send him to... there, maybe he'll have a better life! At least he won't starve to death. A Zhao, think about it, you have to understand me!"

The woman doesn't say anything, staring blankly at Siguan's face, and after a long while, she starts to sob...

And so, the days pass by one by one. Finally, one night. In the tossing and turning of labor pains, in the painful groans, with the help of the neighboring women, amidst the sounds of scissors and water, a new life is finally born into this world, with an endless stream of rebellious and angry, unskilled cries.

"It's a boy, congratulations!" they say.

Siguan's ears can't take these words anymore. "It's finally born," like a heavy burden has been lifted, he breathes a long-held breath; after everyone has left, he uses a brain devoid of sensation and a trembling hand to pick up the newborn child from the bed, says to the woman's head, "A Zhao, you have to understand me!" and then carries the child and rushes out into the dark street.

Outside, it's drizzling, and under the window, he hears the faint sound of the woman's weeping inside the house.

Elizabeth Bergner Stars in "Gone with the Willow" 235

—Nanjing Screening

"Wedding Night" Starts Auspiciously 236

After the "escape" of the rough-lined director Yue Feng, his new work "Wedding Night", after months of careful preparation, officially started work yesterday.

This drama takes modern marriage as its theme, dissecting the virtues and defects of modern marriage, including various aspects of free marriage, old-fashioned marriage, and other issues between men and women.

The distribution of roles in the play is also very interesting. Little actress Yuan Meiyun plays the wife of the fat man Guan Hongda, while the little bird Zhou Xuan plays their maid. There is a very interesting romance in this, that is, what Yuan Meiyun hates the most is her husband Guan Hongda's stupid brain, but Zhou Xuan likes him, so although the stupid Guan is ridiculed by his beautiful wife Yuan Meiyun on one side, he is favored by the delicate maid Zhou Xuan on the other side, so he is the luckiest person in "Wedding Night". In addition, Wang Yin plays a writer. He is dissatisfied with his romantic and modern wife (this role is still being sought) and finally runs away. Later, due to shared feelings, he and Yuan Meiyun announce that they are living together. Therefore, it can be said that "Wedding Night" is not only interesting in the plot, but also very interesting in the distribution of roles.

"Spicy Song" Premieres in Paris 237

The Paris Grand Theater on Avenue Joffre will premiere the Soviet Union's blockbuster "Spicy Song", which was recently transported to China, starting today. The film caused a sensation in the Soviet Union when it was released and won an honorary award. At the same time, it will also screen the newsreel of the All-Union Games with sound dialogue. No detail of the entire event will be missed, which is more complete than the screenings of other companies.

The Inspector General's Fill-in 238

Zhao Dan can be said to be a central figure in the Chinese drama world. This performance of The Inspector General originally had his important scenes, but he was unable to appear on stage after a major illness. It is really a loss on the stage this year. Now, he and Mr. Lai Tian are still acting as stage supervisors, which can be said to be inseparable from the stage even in life and death.

Five days before the performance, Gu Eryi, an important character in The Inspector General, also suddenly suffered from typhoid fever. Fortunately, Dr. Zhang Ziping carefully examined him and he was able to recover. This is really a great fortune among misfortunes.

Recently, it was also heard that Mr. Zhang Ni, one of the directors, has also been overworked in the past month. Fortunately, he did not collapse.

Tracing back to the cause of Zhao Dan's illness, the first effort to rehearse "Nora" was not without some cause. Artists often disregard life in order to pursue the truth and in-depth creation of art. Now, seeing Zhao, Gu, and Zhang's illnesses, it is even more believable.
